PUBLIC COMMENT
During the public comment period, members of the public may speak on general items of interest within the Commission's
jurisdiction that are not on the agenda.  Each member of the public may speak for a maximum of three minutes with a maximum of
15 minutes for the entire public comment period. The Chair shall determine whether the matter is within the Commission's
jurisdiction. The Commission shall not act on or discuss any matters raised during the public comment period, which are not on the
agenda, but shall refer such matters to staff for review and/or request such matters be placed on a future agenda.
PUBLIC HEARING
Planning Commission decisions are final unless appealed to the City Council in accordance with Section 27.08.090 and Section
27.08.060 of the San Mateo Municipal Code. The time within which judicial review of any final decision may be sought is governed by
Code of Civil Procedure section 1094.6. If any person challenges a Planning action in court, they may be limited to raising only those
issues raised at the public hearing or in written correspondence delivered to the City of San Mateo, at or prior to, the public hearing.
Some public hearings will be automatically referred to City Council and those will be indicated below.

SUBJECT:
668 E. 3rd  Avenue – New Multi-Family Residential Development (PA-2025-025)
RECOMMENDATION
Recommend that the City Council adopt a resolution to approve the Site Plan and Architectural Review (SPAR), and Site 
Development Planning Application (SDPA) for the construction of a new multi-family residential building with 128 units and 
associated site improvements at 668 East 3rd Avenue, and find that the Project is Statutorily Exempt from the California 
Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) pursuant to Assembly Bill 130, based on the findings for approval and subject to the 
conditions of approval.  
BACKGROUND:
On April 2, 2025, Prometheus Real Estate Group (applicant) submitted a Planning Application (PA-2025-025) to demolish the 
existing one-story commercial shopping center known as Gateway Crossing (13,650 square feet) and construct a new multi-
family residential building (“Project”). The proposed residential building will be eight stories tall, with one level of below 
grade parking (73 spaces), be approximately 169,750 square feet in size and include 128 residential units. Of the 128 
residential units, 20 are proposed to be provided as below market rate (BMR) affordable housing units (10 at the very low-
income affordability level and 10 at the moderate-income affordability level). The proposed unit mix includes studio, one-
bedroom, two-bedroom and three-bedroom units. This application follows the submittal of a Preliminary Application (PA-
2024-065) made under the Housing Crisis Act (Senate Bill 330) which was submitted on November 13, 2024. A Neighborhood 
Informational Meeting was held by the applicant on March 19, 2025.
Project Site
The Project site is located at 668 East 3rd Avenue, bounded by South Eldorado Street on the east, East 3rd Avenue on the 
north, and South Delaware Street on the west. The site is 0.64 acres (28,387 square feet) in size, has a General Plan Land 
Use designation of Mixed-Use Medium II, and is zoned CBD/S (Central Business District Support). The site is also within the 
Downtown Area Plan Gateway Sub-Area. The existing site is developed with a one-story 13,650 square-foot commercial 
building with surface parking. Adjacent uses include a gas station and office/commercial buildings on the same block just 
south of the Project site, the four-story Metropolitan Apartments complex across South Eldorado Street to the east, a 
currently vacant lot with an approved entitlement for a six-story mixed-use building across South Delaware Street (known 
as “Block 21”) to the west, and a two-story commercial building and gas station/car wash across East 3rd Avenue to the 
north. The downtown San Mateo Caltrain stop is approximately 0.3 miles walking distance from the site to the northwest. 
A location map showing the Project site is included as Attachment 2.
Project Description
The Project includes an eight-story multi-family residential building with 128 residential units and 73 off-street covered 
parking stalls. Of the total 128 units, 20 units are provided as Below Market Rate (BMR) affordable units (10 of which will be

--- page 4 ---

provided at the very-low income affordability level, and the other 10 will be at the moderate income affordability level). The 
unit mix is shown in Table 1 below. The BMR units are distributed throughout each story of the building.

The main pedestrian and street access to the building is at the corner of South Delaware St. and East 3rd Avenue, with 
pedestrian access to the townhouses along East 3rd Avenue.  The parking garage is three levels, with 43 stalls below-grade, 
12 on the ground floor, and 18 on the second story. Bicycle parking facilities include 140 long-term secured bicycle storage 
racks located within the parking areas, and exterior bike racks to accommodate the required 10 short-term bicycle parking 
spaces are provided along South Delaware Street. The Project proposes a variety of residential amenities, including a fitness 
room with a sauna and strength studio, dog washing area, amenity deck on the third floor, and a common room and amenity 
deck with a barbeque area on the eighth floor. 
The building design and context are discussed further below. Project plans showing the proposed site plan, floor plans, 
elevations, and architectural renderings are included as Attachment 3.
APPLICABLE CODE AND POLICY REVIEW:
General Plan and Zoning Code
The  General Plan 2040 Land Use Designation for the Project site is Mixed Use Medium II, which allows for medium-density 
mixed-use buildings that provide a mix of commercial, office, and/or residential uses within the same site or building.  This 
Land Use Designation allows for a mix of uses near other mixed-use, commercial, or residential areas, and within Downtown. 
The Mixed-Use Medium II designation allows for residential densities of up to 99 dwelling units per acre. For this 0.64-acre 
site, the base density allows up to 64 units. (The calculation of 63.36 units that is rounded up to 64 units in accordance with 
State housing law requiring fractional units be rounded up to the nearest whole number). To achieve the total of 128 units, 
which is double the maximum density, the applicant is requesting a density bonus under State law, which is further discussed 
below. A list of applicable General Plan policies, and discussion of how the Project is consistent with these policies is included 
in the Resolution (Attachment 1).
The Project site is zoned Central Business District Support (CBD/S), which is subject to development standards outlined in 
San Mateo Municipal Code (“SMMC”) Chapter 27.39. The CBD/S district allows for a variety of uses (both commercial and 
residential) and is intended to encourage opportunities for businesses that support the downtown core, and residential uses 
to support housing opportunities close to the downtown. A Project Data Table listing the applicable Zoning Code standards 
and the Project’s conformance to them Is included as Attachment 4. As noted in the table, where there is an inconsistency 
between the Zoning Code and the General Plan 2040, the General Plan shall control (per Government Code Section 
65860(c)(2)(B) and SMMC Section 27.02.220). Additionally, the applicant has not requested any concessions, but is seeking 
waivers to certain development standards in accordance with State Density Bonus Law (Government Code Section 65915). 
These waivers are discussed in greater detail below. 
Parking Standards
The Project is located within the City’s Central Parking Improvement District, which was established to set specific parking 
1 “Urban 1-bed” are designed to be a type of studio unit, with a partial wall separating the living and sleeping areas. Since the separation is not a full wall, this is not 
counted as a bedroom.
2 Of the five 3-bedroom units, one is a 3-bedroom apartment unit with one level, and the other four are the 3-bedroom “townhome” style units, which have two levels 
of living area and are accessible by separate entrances at the ground level. The one very-low income 3-bed BMR unit is a townhome style unit.

--- page 5 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
regulations for projects located within the Downtown Specific Plan Area.  However, the site is also located within 0.5-miles 
of the Downtown San Mateo Caltrain station, which is a major transit stop. Pursuant to Government Code Section 65863.2 
(AB 2097), the Project is not subject to minimum parking requirements or parking in-lieu fees. Despite the fact that no 
parking is required, the proposed Project does include 73 off-street parking stalls for the residents.  
Downtown Area Plan
The Project site is located within the Downtown Plan Area, in the Gateway Sub-Area. The Downtown Area Plan, adopted in 
2009, provides a vision for Downtown San Mateo that is pedestrian-friendly and serves as a focal point of the community, 
including a blend of historical buildings and new development, with retail, entertainment, and housing opportunities. The 
Gateway Sub-Area serves as the primary entry point to Downtown from U.S. Highway 101. The vision of the Gateway Sub-
Area includes an emphasis on multi-family residential uses, with design guidelines aimed at promoting new development 
that is compatible with existing neighborhoods. The Downtown and Gateway design guidelines have been adapted to 
enforceable objective standards reflected in the City’s Multifamily and Residential Mixed-Use Objective Design Standards 
(ODS), discussed further below. 
Site Plan and Architectural Review (SPAR)
The Project requires a Site Plan and Architectural Review (SPAR) approval for construction of a new building in accordance 
with SMMC Section 27.08.030. Staff have reviewed the Project for compliance with the Objective Design Standards and 
worked with the applicant to revise portions of the design for greater compatibility with these standards and the surrounding 
neighborhood context. Detailed findings for approval of the SPAR are included in the Resolution (Attachment 1). 
Site Development Planning Application (SDPA)
The Project requires a Site Development Planning Application (SDPA) for removal of major vegetation in conjunction with 
the redevelopment. The Project is exempt from the SDPA requirements related to grading activities per SMMC Section 
23.40.030(d)(1), as the excavations below finished grade proposed for this Project are for building footings and a basement 
level parking structure within the footprint of the building. “Major vegetation” is defined as live vegetation consisting of tree 
growth with a trunk diameter of six inches or greater measured at 54-inches above natural grade. Additionally, the Municipal 
Code defines a “Protected Tree” as any heritage tree or street tree. Heritage trees include any oak tree with a minimum 
diameter of 10 inches measured at 54-inches above natural grade, as well as any other tree species with a minimum diameter 
of 15 inches measured at 54-inches above natural grade. 
On the Project site there are a total of nine existing trees, four of which qualify as protected trees. As a part of the Project 
plans, all of the existing trees are proposed to be removed. Per SMMC Section 27.71, the Project is required to provide the 
equivalent landscape unit (LU) value of the removed trees, either by planting new trees, paying an in-lieu fee, or providing 
some combination of both new tree planting and in-lieu fee payment. The Project proposes to plant 16 new trees along the 
Project frontages, and will pay an in-lieu fee into the City’s Tree Planting Fund for the difference between the loss of LU 
value and tree replacement credit. Additional details on the SDPA findings for approval are included in the Resolution 
(Attachment 1). 
APPLICABLE HOUSING LAWS:
State Density Bonus Law
The Project utilizes the provisions of State Density Bonus Law in accordance with Government Code Section 65915 and as 
locally adopted in SMMC Chapter 27.15 Density Bonus. To comply with Density Bonus regulations, the City must allow for 
increased residential density, reduced parking standards, and “concessions” and “waivers” from development standards for 
residential projects that provide a certain percentage of units as affordable units.
The Project site’s General Plan Land Use Designation of Mixed-Use Medium II, with a density of 99 units per acre, allows for  
a base of 64 units. The Project includes 15 percent (10 units) at the very low-income level, and another 15 percent (10 units) 
at the moderate-income level. Pursuant to AB 1287 (Government Code Section 66915(v)), a project can receive a 50 percent 
density bonus when 15 percent of the units are proposed at very low-income levels and another 50 percent density bonus 
when an additional 15 percent moderate rate units are added. This would afford the Project a “stacked” density bonus of 
up to 100 percent, which allows for a maximum of 128 units.

--- page 6 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Concession and Waiver Requests
For this Project, State Density Bonus Law also allows the applicant to request up to three concessions and unlimited waivers 
from development standards. Generally speaking, a concession (or incentive) is a reduction or modification of a development 
standard that results in identifiable or actual cost reductions to provide for affordable housing costs, helping to make the 
Project financially feasible. (A concession also includes a reduction in site development standards or a modification of zoning 
code requirements that exceed minimum building standards, as specified.)  A waiver is a modification of a standard that 
would otherwise physically preclude the construction of the Project at the allowed density. The Project application does not 
identify any concession requests under State Density Bonus Law. However, the Project is seeking several waivers for aspects 
of the Project that do not meet various City development standards. The applicant has also included a summary of the 
Project waivers in a density bonus request letter (Attachment 5), as well as waiver diagrams on Sheets G010 and G011 of 
the Project plans (Attachment 3). A complete list of the Project waivers is included in Attachment 1, Exhibit B.
Staff have evaluated the waivers and concluded that the waivers identified are necessary to allow construction of the Project 
at the densities permitted under the City’s General Plan and State Density Bonus Law. 
Other Applicable State Laws
In addition to State Density Bonus Law, there are several other State Laws that regulate housing development projects. For 
this Project, these include, but are not necessarily limited to the following:
•
The Housing Crisis Act (Senate Bill 330)
o
Under Senate Bill 330 (SB 330), the Project vests the ordinances, policies, and standards adopted and in 
effect when a preliminary application was submitted to the City. This Project submitted a Preliminary 
Application under SB 330 on November 13, 2024, and is therefore vested to the ordinances, policies, and 
standards in place as of this date. 
•
The Housing Accountability Act (HAA) 
o
The HAA limits a local agency’s ability to deny, reduce the density of, or render housing development 
projects infeasible if objective standards are met. As proposed, this Project meets all applicable objective 
standards in the General Plan, Zoning Code, and other local policy documents that were in effect at the time 
the preliminary application was submitted under SB330.
•
Assembly Bill 130
o
Assembly Bill 130 (AB 130) was signed into law and became effective immediately on June 20, 2025. AB130 
included numerous changes related to housing laws, including the addition of a new statutory exemption 
from the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) for housing development projects on sites under 20 
acres that meet specific qualifying criteria. In addition to the CEQA exemption, AB130 requires the Project 
to be processed on an expedited timeline.  
Inclusionary Housing Requirements
The City’s Below Market Rate (Inclusionary) Program requires rental projects of 11 or more units to provide a minimum of 
15 percent of the proposed units to be designated low-income units. The applicant proposes to designate 10 units (15 
percent of the base density) as affordable at the very low-income level, which meets the City’s Inclusionary Program 
requirements. These affordable units are required to be distributed throughout the development, have access to all on-site 
amenities, generally be of comparable size to similar market rate units, and have an exterior design and appearance 
compatible with similar market rate units.
DESIGN REVIEW – OBJECTIVE DESIGN STANDARDS:
The Project was reviewed for consistency with the City’s Multi-family and Residential Mixed-Use Objective Design Standards 
(ODS). The Project’s architectural style includes influences of Mediterranean and Spanish Revival styles, expressed in a 
contemporary manner. Features such as arches and decorative tile around the entryway, balconies, pergolas in open space 
areas, as well as materials such as stucco, metal railings, and terra-cotta roof tiles are incorporated into the design, which 
also features more modern window openings and massing.
The building is eight stories in height, which is considered a high-rise building per the City’s ODS. The Project includes a

--- page 7 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
parking structure, with one basement level and parking integrated into the building on the first two levels. The parking area 
is fully enclosed, with one garage entry from South Eldorado Street proposed. The frontage includes public open space with 
landscape planters and a seating bench incorporated into the design, as well as ground-level residential entries for four 
townhome units along East 3rd Avenue, contributing to a pedestrian-friendly environment at the street level. The structure’s 
massing follows the rule of thirds, with three primary horizontal elements, as well as a distinct base, body, and top to provide 
vertical massing breaks. The Project also requests several waivers from the ODS, specifically related to blank walls, and 
standards derived from the Downtown Plan Area and Vision of the Gateway related to façade design, residential entries, 
massing and articulation, setbacks, step backs, height, and architectural styles and materials. 
TRANSPORTATION ANALYSIS:
The Project is exempt from Vehicle Miles Travelled (VMT) analysis pursuant to AB 130, which establishes a statutory 
exemption for qualifying infill projects from the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA). The Project’s eligibility under 
this exemption is discussed further below. 
The project was reviewed by staff, consistent with the General Plan, for compliance with the City’s Local Transportation 
Analysis Guidelines to address potential impacts to traffic operations. Trip generation data was provided by the applicant 
and peer reviewed by staff. The existing land use, including the convenience store and restaurants on site generates an 
estimated 124 trips in the AM peak hour, whereas the proposed residential creates an estimated 47 trips in the AM peak 
hour. For the PM peak hour, the existing land uses generate an estimated 140 trips, whereas the proposed residential use is 
estimated to generate only 50 trips5. Therefore, based on the difference between the existing and proposed land uses, the 
project will result in a net decrease in both AM and PM peak hour trips. Based on this analysis, the project is not expected 
to have significant impacts to local traffic operations. 
The initial Project submittal included two driveway entrances, one on South Delaware Street and another on South Eldorado 
Street. In accordance with Zoning Code Section 27.64.025, new driveway access on arterial streets is prohibited unless no 
other means of access is available. Therefore, the Project was redesigned to adjust the vehicular access to one driveway off 
of South Eldorado Street, which is a local street.
NOTICE PROVIDED:
All meeting noticing requirements were met. The Project was noticed per Section 27.08.050 of the Zoning Code, with mailed 
notices sent to owners and residents within 1,000 feet of the Project site, and City placards posted on the Project site 10 
days prior to the public hearing. In addition to the required noticing, public hearing information for the Project was included 
in an issue of the bi-weekly Planning E-newsletter circulated prior to the hearing date. 
PUBLIC COMMENTS:
The applicant held a formal Neighborhood Informational Meeting on March 19, 2025, which was attended by approximately 
40 participants. The discussion and comments at the Neighborhood Informational Meeting included clarifying questions 
about the Project, which were answered by the developer, as well as public comments focused on concerns about parking 
adequacy, traffic and construction impacts, and the loss of existing businesses/retail. During the formal application review, 
no additional public comments were submitted to staff. Any public comments received after the publication of this report 
will be forward to the Planning Commission for review and consideration and posted to this item on the City’s Agendas & 
Minutes Public Meeting Portal as “Post Packet Public Comments.”

time of the application filing date, including the ones listed below, which are assessed and collected prior to the issuance of 
building permits or occupancy6:

improvement cost) in-lieu of providing on-site public art.
•
Transportation Improvement Fee of approximately $479,000 to fund citywide traffic improvements.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
In accordance with the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA), the Project meets the criteria to be statutorily exempt 
from further environmental review pursuant to Public Resources Code Section 21080.66. This exemption was enacted as a 
part of Assembly Bill 130 (AB130), effective as of June 30, 2025. The applicant has provided a memo detailing the Project’s 
qualification under AB130, included as Attachment 6. Staff have reviewed the eligibility criteria and determined that the 
Project meets the qualifying criteria under AB 130.
In accordance with Public Resources Code Section 21080.66(b)(1)(A), the City formally noticed Native American tribes for 
consultation regarding the Project and its potential impacts on tribal cultural resources. One tribe responded to the City’s 
notice to request consultation. The Project Conditions of Approval (Attachment 1, Exhibit A) include conditions required to 
satisfy requirements of AB 130 to avoid impacts to tribal cultural resources. In addition, consistent with Public Resources 
Code 21080.66(c), the Project Conditions of Approval include a requirement for the applicant to complete a phase I 
environmental assessment, and to mitigate any hazards as required per the statute.

RESOLUTION NO. 
 (2026)
A RESOLUTION OF THE PLANNING COMMISSION TO RECOMMEND THAT THE CITY COUNCIL APPROVE A 
PLANNING APPLICATION TO CONSTRUCT 128 RESIDENTIAL UNITS AND ASSOCIATED SITE IMPROVEMENTS, 
AND DETERMINE THAT THE PROJECT IS EXEMPT FROM FURTHER ENVIRONMENTAL REVIEW UNDER 
CALIFORNIA ENVIRONMENTAL QUALITY ACT
WHEREAS, Prometheus Real Estate Group (herein referred to as the “Applicant”) submitted a Planning 
Application No. PA-2025-025 for a Site Plan and Architectural Review and Site Development Planning Application 
for construction of a new multi-family development with 128 rental residential units and associated off-street 
parking, landscaping and open space areas located 668 E 3rd Ave (collectively referred to as “Project”) in the City 
of San Mateo (“City”);
WHEREAS, the proposed Project is designated as Mixed-Use Medium II in the General Plan Land Use Plan, 
Zoned Central Business District Support (CBD/S) in the Zoning Ordinance, and located within Downtown Area Plan 
– Gateway Sub Area planning area;
WHEREAS, in fulfillment of the City’s Below Market Rate requirement pursuant to SMMC Section 
27.16.050, the Project is providing ten (10) rental units affordable to very-low income households, of which four 
are “urban one-bedroom" units, three are one-bedroom units, two are two-bedroom units, and one is a three-
bedroom unit. The project is additionally providing ten (10) rental units affordable to moderate income 
households pursuant to Government Code Section 65915 et. seq;
WHEREAS, the San Mateo Municipal Code (“SMMC”) Section 27.06.050 authorizes the City Council to take 
final action on Site Plan and Architectural Review for buildings that exceed the height limit in the General Plan;
WHEREAS, the Project is exempt from CEQA under Public Resource Code 21080.66, based on the findings 
listed below;
WHEREAS, the Project is consistent with the applicable policies of the General Plan 2040 and other 
applicable policies;
WHEREAS, the Project is providing 15 percent of the units affordable to very-low income households, 
which allows the applicant to request up to three concessions and unlimited waivers from development 
standards pursuant to Government Code Section 65915(d). The Project does not request any concessions. A list 
of Project waivers is included as Exhibit B; and
WHEREAS, the Planning Commission held a public hearing for the Project on February 10, 2026, duly 
noticed, at which all public comments were considered.
NOW, THEREFORE, THE PLANNING COMMISSION OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO, CALIFORNIA, HEREBY 
FINDS AND RESOLVES that:

1.
The Planning Commission recommends approval of the Project to the City Council.

The Planning Commission finds on the basis of the whole record before it that the Project will not 
have a significant effect on the environment and is therefore statutory exempt from the 
provisions of CEQA under Public Resource Code Section 21080.66 (AB 130), as follows:
a.
The Project is consistent with the General Plan land use designation and all applicable General 
Plan policies as well as the applicable zoning designation of CBS/S;
b.
The Project site is located within the City of San Mateo on a Project site less than 20 acres 
(0.64 acres) that is surrounded by urban uses;
c.
The site has been previously developed with an urban use;
d.
The Project provides 200 dwelling units per acre, which exceeds one-half of the Housing 
Element’s default density threshold of 99 dwelling units per acre for accommodating lower-
income households.
e.
The Project is not located within a coastal zone, prime farmland or farmland of statewide 
importance, wetland, very high fire hazard severity zone, hazardous waste site, delineated 
earthquake fault zone, special flood hazard area, regulatory floodway, lands identified for 
conservation in an adopted natural community conservation plan, or habitat for protected 
species;
f.
The Project does not involve the demolition of a historic structure listed on a national, state, 
or local register prior to the application submittal;
g.
No portion of the Project is designated for use as a hotel, motel, bed and breakfast inn, or 
other transient lodging;
h.
The Project is not located within 500 feet of the freeway;
i.
The Project completed tribal consultation pursuant to Public Resources Code Section 
21080.66(b)(1), with one tribe participating in the consultation process. Appropriate 
conditions are included in the Conditions of Approval to ensure the avoidance of impacts to 
cultural resources.
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, BY THE PLANNING COMMISSION OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO, CALIFORNIA AS 
FOLLOWS:
General Plan Conformance
3.
The Project conforms to applicable policies of the General Plan 2040 Land Use Element.
a.
Policy LU 1.1 Equitable Development. Prioritize development projects that meet social and 
economic needs of the economically vulnerable populations to address and reverse the 
underlying socioeconomic factors in the community that contribute to residential and social 
segregation in the city. Provide a range of housing types, sizes, and affordability levels in all 
San Mateo neighborhoods.
b.
Policy LU 3.1 Housing Diversity. Promote safe, attractive, and walkable residential 
neighborhoods with diverse types and sizes of homes for individuals, families, and households 
of all income levels.

--- page 11 ---


--- page 12 ---
The Project is consistent with the above Land Use Element policies by providing a diverse set of 
units ranging from studio to three-bedrooms, including 108 market-rate units and 20 affordable 
units for (10 for very-low income households and 10 for moderate income households), within 
one-half mile of the Downtown San Mateo Caltrain Station. The Project replaces a one-story 
commercial building with high-quality residential development that incorporates on-site 
amenities and open spaces. It also includes a range of bedroom configurations that support 
family-oriented living, including two- and three-bedroom units.
4.
The Project conforms to applicable policies of the General Plan 2040 Circulation Element.
a.
Policy C 3.2 Pedestrian Enhancements with New Development. Require new development 
projects to provide sidewalks and pedestrian ramps and to repair or replace damaged 
sidewalks, in addition to right-of-way improvements identified in adopted City master plans. 
Encourage new developments to include pedestrian-oriented design to facilitate pedestrian 
path of travel.
b.
Policy C 4.5 Bicycle Improvements. Require new developments to construct or contribute to 
improvements that enhance the cyclist experience, including bicycle lanes and bicycle 
parking.
The Project is consistent with the above Circulation Element policies by providing sidewalks and 
pedestrian path of travel in accordance with the City’s Pedestrian Master Plan. The Project 
incorporates street-level landscaping as well as a public open space with bench seating near the 
entry of the building. In addition, the Project provides both short-term and long-term bicycle 
parking.
5.
The Project conforms to applicable policies of Housing Element 2023-02031.
a.
Policy H 1.5 Encourage Family Housing. Prioritize creation of housing that addresses the 
needs of large families, providing greater housing choice.
b.
Policy H1.3 Increase Affordable Housing Production. Adopting an updated Density 
Bonus/Community Benefit Program that provides additional incentives and/or streamlining 
option for housing projects that provide additional affordable units or the most needed unit 
types (including those with special needs) beyond minimum State requirements.
c.
Policy H 1.12 Encourage Development of Missing Middle Housing.
The Project is consistent with the applicable Housing Element policies by providing family-sized 
housing, including units with two- and three-bedroom floor plans. The Project increases 
affordable housing production by providing 20 affordable units for (10 for very-low income 
households and 10 for moderate income households). In addition, the Project includes 128 total 
units, expanding housing options for a range of household sizes and income levels.
6.
The Project conforms to applicable policies of the General Plan 2040 Community Design and 
Historic Resources Element.
a.
Policy CD 3.2 Replacement Planting. Require appropriate replacement planting or payment 
of an in-lieu fee when protected trees on public or private property are removed.
b.
Policy CD 4.3 Tribal Consultation. Consult with Native American representatives, including 
through early coordination, to identify locations of importance to Native Americans, including 
archaeological sites, sacred sites, traditional cultural properties, and other types of tribal 
cultural resources. Respect tribal concerns if a tribe has a religious prohibition against 
revealing information about specific practices or locations.
c.
Policy CD 6.7 Public Open Space Design. Seek opportunities to establish public open spaces 
in new developments and new public buildings, and promote innovative and creative designs

--- page 13 ---


--- page 14 ---
to create exceptional, unique, and functional spaces. Require signage that clearly delineates 
these spaces as publicly accessible.
d.
Policy CD 7.3 Multifamily Design. Encourage architectural design of new multifamily 
developments that enhances a neighborhood’s visual and architectural character by providing 
context sensitive building and pedestrian-scale elements, high-quality materials and 
construction, open space, and resident amenities.
The Project provides in-lieu fees for protected trees proposed for removal and includes the 
installation of replacement trees in accordance with City requirements. Tribal consultation for the 
Project was completed, and appropriate conditions are included in the Conditions of Approval to 
ensure the avoidance of impacts to cultural resources. The Project incorporates on-site open 
space areas with amenities, including a ground level entry plaza, private balconies per unit, 
common open space amenity decks at the third and eighth stories, a fitness center, common 
room, and bicycle parking. In addition, the Project proposes a contemporary Mediterranean and 
Spanish-inspired architectural style that enhances neighborhood character and includes 
pedestrian-scale elements such as a seating area and landscaping, as well as resident-serving 
amenities.
Downtown Area Plan
a.
In conformance with Policy I.3, the Project proposes a well-designed contemporary building 
influenced by Mediterranean and Spanish Revival styles at an appropriate building scale and 
massing, which serves as a landmark entrance to the downtown core along 3rd Avenue from 
east of the railroad corridor. The Project also integrates sidewalks, street trees, landscaping 
and a public seating area to further enhance pedestrian activity along 3rd Avenue, Delaware 
Street, and Eldorado Street.
b.
In conformance with Policies II.7 and III.8, the Project includes pedestrian-scale improvements 
through new landscaping, bicycle parking, and street trees consistent with the Street Tree 
Master Plan.
c.
The Project conforms to Policy II.0, Housing in the Retail Core, by creating new housing units 
within close proximity to the downtown area and Caltrain station.
d.
The reduced setbacks, increased building height, and varied stepbacks the Project 
incorporates are allowed as waiver requests under State Density Bonus Law (California 
Government Code Section 665915).
Site Plan and Architectural Review (SPAR)
1.
The Site Plan and Architectural Review (Municipal Code Section 27.08.030) application and 
associated Conditions of Approval are approved based on the following findings:
a.
The structures, site plan, and landscaping are in scale and harmonious with the character of 
the neighborhood in that:
i.
The design and massing of the proposed buildings are appropriately scaled and 
compatible with the existing surrounding uses, which include an existing four-story 
multifamily apartment building to the east, a proposed six-story mixed use building 
to the west, and commercial/office buildings to the south and north.
ii.
The Project proposes a high-quality, contemporary Mediterranean and Spanish-
Revival inspired design, incorporating materials and details emblematic of these

--- page 15 ---


--- page 16 ---
architectural styles that positively enhance the existing character of the 
neighborhood and surrounding area.
iii.
The Project provides site plan and landscape improvements that contribute to a 
welcoming and comfortable pedestrian experience, serving as an entry point to 
Downtown.
b.
The development will not be detrimental to the harmonious and orderly growth of the City in 
that:
i.
The Project has voluntarily included 76 off-street parking spaces, despite being 
exempted from minimum parking standards under State law, to accommodate 
expected demand for residential parking, in addition to implementing Transportation 
Demand Management measures through the C/CAG checklist.
ii.
The Project is consistent with the General Plan, Zoning Code, Downtown Area Plan, 
and the Multi-Family and Residential Mixed-Use Objective Design Standards, except 
where modifications are allowed under the State Density Bonus Law.
iii.
The Project is in conformance with the Bicycle Master Plan and the Citywide 
Pedestrian Master Plan.
c.
The development will not impair the desirability of investment or occupation in the vicinity, 
and otherwise is in the best interests of the public health, safety, or welfare in that:
i.
The Project provides additional housing opportunities including affordable housing 
units and, as conditioned, would not result in any significant impacts to public health, 
safety, or welfare.
ii.
The Project will be constructed in compliance with all applicable building codes, fire 
codes, and the City’s building security requirements.
d.
The development meets all applicable standards as adopted by the Planning Commission and 
City Council, conforms with the General Plan, and will correct any violations of the zoning 
ordinance, building code, or other municipal codes that exist on the site, in that:
i.
The Project complies with applicable General Plan, Zoning Code, Downtown Area 
Specific Plan, and Objective Design Standards, subject to approval of the identified 
waivers under State Density Bonus Law. No violations of the Zoning Ordinance or 
Building Code were identified on the site. Therefore, the development meets all 
applicable standards as adopted by the Planning Commission and City Council, 
conforms with the General Plan and other applicable plans and policies.
e.
The development will not adversely affect matters regarding police protection, crime 
prevention, and security in that the buildings, paths of travel, and parking facilities will be 
required to conform to the City’s current Security Ordinance through Conditions of Approval, 
in that:

--- page 17 ---


--- page 18 ---
i.
The Project complies with the City’s Security Ordinance by providing a physical 
security plan and a site lighting plan through the Conditions of Approval, which are 
intended to promote crime prevention.
Site Development Planning Application (SDPA)
The project grading activities are exempt from the requirements for Site Development Planning 
Application per San Mateo Municipal Code Section 23.40.030(d)(1), as the excavations below finished 
grade proposed for this project are for building footings and a basement level parking structure within the 
footprint of the building. Therefore, the Site Development Planning Application review is limited to the 
major vegetation removal proposed.
All concerns regarding major vegetation removal have been addressed and the Site Development Planning 
Application (SMMC Section 23.40.040) and associated Conditions of Approval are approved based on the 
following findings and factors:
a.
Whether the natural landscape and major vegetation is unnecessarily scarred through the 
proposed grading or removal of vegetation;
i. The Project will not scar the natural landscape or major vegetation as a result of the 
proposed grading or vegetation removal.
b.
The report from the Project Arborist with respect to Protected Trees pursuant to SMMC 
Chapters 27.71 and 13.40;
i.
The Project will result in the removal of nine existing trees, of which four are 
considered protected trees. The removal of these trees is necessary to accommodate 
the development of the proposed Project. All trees will be removed and replaced with 
appropriate landscaping to both enhance the site and create necessary buffers 
between surrounding properties.
ii.All concerns regarding tree removal on the site have been addressed as conditions of 
approval requiring conformance to the City's landscape regulations, through the 
provision of new tree planting as shown on the project plans, and/or through the 
payment of a fee to the City’s tree planting fund.

complete a preliminary endangerment assessment, as defined in Section 78095 of 
the Health and Safety Code, prepared by an environmental assessor to determine 
the existence of any release of a hazardous substance on the site and to determine 
the potential for exposure of future occupants to significant health hazards from 
any nearby property or activity.

be removed, or any effects of the release shall be mitigated to levels required by 
current federal and state statutory and regulatory standards before the local 
government issues a certificate of occupancy.
c.
If a potential for exposure to significant hazards from surrounding properties or 
activities is found to exist, the effects of the potential exposure shall be mitigated 
to levels required by current federal and state statutory and regulatory standards
before the local government issues a certificate of occupancy. (PLANNING)

40 RESIDENTIAL PARKING GARAGE SECURITY – The building permit plans for the 
superstructure shall show:
A. Restricted access to the parking garage with electrically operated closures to allow 
passage of motor vehicles at all times. The closures, whether overhead, sliding or 
swinging shall be provided with reopening devices which will function to stop and 
reopen the closure in case the closure is obstructed when closing. Openings into 
the garage which are not for vehicular or human passage shall be provided with 
security grilles or screens.
B. Digital keypads shall be provided to allow for entry by services and emergency 
services vehicles into the garages at all times. Exterior doors or gates providing 
access into the secure areas of the parking garage shall remain locked at all times, 
and shall only be accessible through the use of keys, key fob or remote keyless 
entry system devices furnished to the building residents. Pedestrian access points 
exiting out of garage shall also be accessible through the use of keys furnished to 
the building residents and shall be equipped with self-closing devices. All storage, 
maintenance, and trash rooms within parking garages shall have doors which 
cannot be locked from the inside, and that close and lock quickly and automatically 
upon exit.
C. Parking spaces shall not be numbered to coincide with interior unit numbers.
D. Lighting in the parking garage shall be in conformance with the Security Ordinance 
as it applies to SITE LIGHTING. No dark areas shall exist inside the parking garage 
(POLICE)

43 DRAINAGE – The building permit plans show drainage designed into landscaping with the 
purpose of reducing volume or improving quality of runoff from the site shall be 
implemented, to the extent feasible, subject to the approval of the Director of Public 
Works or designee. Where necessary, sidewalk drains per City Standard Drawings shall be 
provided to direct the water under the sidewalk and through the curb. No increase to the 
peak discharge shall be permitted downstream. In addition, discharge shall conform to any 
non point source permit issued by the Regional Water Quality Control Board. Drainage 
improvements made on-site shall conform to standard engineering practices and shall not 
allow any site drainage to impact adjacent properties. All drainage capacity calculations 
shall be performed by a licensed Civil Engineer, whose signed engineer’s stamp shall 
appear on the calculations sheets and shall be submitted to the City for review and 
approval with the project civil plans submitted as part of the building permit for the 
superstructure. Projects that include permanent structural controls for stormwater 
treatment, shall comply with requirements of Section C.3 of the Municipal Regional 
Stormwater Permit for San Mateo County (MRP). The O&M (operation and maintenance) 
procedures for such control features shall be submitted for review and approval prior to 
occupancy and specify the owner’s responsibility to ensure their ongoing effective 
operation and maintenance. Such O&M responsibility requirements shall be recorded with 
the County of San Mateo Recorder’s Office. The building permit plans for the 
superstructure shall show drainage. (PUBLIC WORKS)

71 PALEONTOLOGICAL RESOURCES – In the event of the discovery of paleontological 
resources (fossils) whether on-site or in the public right-of-way, the applicant shall halt all 
construction activities within 50 feet of the discovery, notify the Planning Manager and/or 
Project Planner, and retain a qualified paleontologist to determine the significance of the 
discovery. The paleontologist shall evaluate the uniqueness of the find, prepare a written 
report documenting the find and recommending further courses of action, and submit a 
summary of findings to the Project Planner. The applicant shall incorporate the 
recommendations of the paleontologist when continuing construction. (PLANNING)

81 GROUND WATER DISCHARGE – In accordance with the Director of Public Works 
Groundwater Discharge Policy, discharge of contaminated groundwater to the sanitary 
sewer is only allowed on a temporary basis and will not be permitted for a period greater 
than 6 months. Discharges for longer than 6 months shall obtain an NPDES permit from 
the State Water Board to discharge to the storm drain system. Discharge of 
uncontaminated groundwater to the storm drain is permissible if the applicant can 
provide analytical data to support the claim. No discharge to the storm drain shall be 
allowed without prior approval from the Public Works Department. All discharges to the 
sanitary sewer (contaminated and uncontaminated) require a Waste Discharge Permit and 
shall comply with the City’s discharge limits. (PUBLIC WORKS)
82 HOLIDAY CONSTRUCTION MORATORIUM – Due to concerns for businesses within the 
vicinity of Hillsdale Mall and within the Downtown area during the holiday season 
(Monday prior to Thanksgiving to January 1), there shall be no construction activities 
within the right-of-way which would create lane closures, eliminate parking, create 
pedestrian detours, or other activities that may create a major disturbance as determined 
by the Director of Public Works or designee. Exceptions to this condition shall be made in 
writing to the Public Works Director or designee. For Hillsdale Shopping Center, the 
construction prohibition streets shall include Hillsdale Boulevard between U.S. 101 and SR 
92, 31st Avenue between El Camino Real and Hacienda Street, and Edison Street and 
Hacienda Street in the vicinity of the shopping center. For purposes of this condition, the 
limits of the Downtown area shall be defined as: between El Camino Real on the west and 
Delaware Street on the east, Tilton Avenue on the north, and Fifth Avenue on the south. 
The prohibition shall also include the 3rd and 4th Avenue corridors between Delaware 
Street and U.S. 101. (PUBLIC WORKS)

84 PUBLIC WORKS CONSTRUCTION ACTIVITIES – The following provision to control traffic 
congestion, noise, and dust shall be followed during site excavation, grading and 
construction:
(A) Construction activities related to the issuance of any Public Works permit shall be 
restricted to the weekday between 7:00 a.m. and 7:00 p.m. Please note, however, that no 
work shall be allowed to take place within the City right-of-way after 5:00 p.m. In addition, 
no work being done under the issuance of a Public Works encroachment permit may be 
performed on the weekend unless prior approvals have been granted by Public Works. 
Earth haul and materials delivery to and from the site, including truck arrivals and 
departures to and from the site, will be prohibited between the weekday hours of 4:00
p.m. 5:30 p.m. Signs outlining these restrictions shall be posted at conspicuous locations 
on site. The signs shall be per the City Standard Drawing for posting construction hours. 
The sign shall be kept free of graffiti at all times. Contact the Public Works Department to 
obtain sample City Standard sign outlining hours of operation.
The allowed hours of Public Works construction activities may be waived or modified 
through an exemption, for limited periods, if the Director of Public Works or designee 
finds that:
(i) The following criteria are met:

(a) Permitting extended hours of construction will decrease the total time needed to

(b) Permitting extended hours of construction are required to accommodate design or

safety. If such a condition exists, the City may waive any of the remaining requirements 
outlined below.

City to mitigate significant impacts.
(iii) The contractor or owner of the property will notify residential and commercial 
occupants of property adjacent to the construction site of the hours of construction 
activity which may impact the area. This notification shall be provided three days prior to 
the start of the extended construction activity.
(iv) The approved hours of construction activity will be posted at the construction site in a 
place and manner that can be easily viewed by any interested member of the public.
The Director of Public Works or designee may revoke the exemption at any time if the 
contractor or owner of the property fails to abide by the conditions of exemption or if it is 
determined that the peace, comfort and tranquility of the occupants of adjacent 
residential or commercial properties are impaired because of the location and nature of 
the construction. The waiver application shall be submitted to the Public Works 
Construction Inspector ten (10) working days prior to the requested date of waiver.
(B) All construction vehicles shall be properly maintained and equipped with exhaust 
mufflers that meet State standards.
(C) Newly disturbed soil surfaces shall be watered down regularly by a water trucks or by 
other approved method maintained on site during all grading operations. Construction

99 VIDEO SURVEILLANCE STANDARDS – To the extent permitted by applicable law, the

subject to the following requirements:

captured video material shall be accessible to investigating police personnel through some 
form of facility management during regular business hours. The applicant shall provide 
proof of registration of the video surveillance camera system with the City through the 
City’s Neighborhood Eyes Security Team web form (https://sanmateoconnect.org/).
(B) Cameras shall be placed and maintained to view common areas of the property 
accessible to the public such as lobbies, parking lots, parking garages and entrances and 
exits to all parking garages, gates dividing different uses inside mixed-use parking garages, 
driveways, circulation areas, aisles, passageways, recesses, and grounds contiguous to all 
buildings. This condition is not intended to require Applicant to install pole mount 
cameras on the property, cameras to view these areas may be installed on the building 
facing out.
(C) The cameras in this system shall be megapixel or better CCTV cameras that shall be 
capable of operating in all lighting conditions anticipated at project completion. Cameras 
viewing locations intended to allow routine vehicle passage onto the sites and/or garages 
shall additionally be capable of capturing the front and rear of all entering and exiting 
vehicles that use the sites and/or garages, and be of sufficient quality to identify the make 
and model of vehicles accessing the site, clearly read both front and rear license plates of 
vehicles, and clearly depict faces of occupants through the front windshield. (POLICE)

EXHIBIT B
SUMMARY OF PROJECT WAIVERS
The waivers to the following standards have been identiﬁed, to be applied pursuant to State Density Bonus
Law:
1)
Loading Berth – Per SMMC Section 27.64.390, the project requires a minimum loading zone berth 
of 10’x25’. The proposed loading zone is 8’x25’.
2)
Turning Radii – Per SMMC Section 27.64.130, turning aisles or ramps with two-way traﬃc shall 
have radii and aisle widths suﬃcient for 2 or more automobiles to pass on the turn. The proposed 
project includes turning radii that are less that the code requirements. The applicant has provided 
a turning diagram to demonstrate functionality of the proposed ramp.
3)
Building Height – Per the San Mateo General Plan 2040, the Mixed Use Medium II land use 
designation allows for residential buildings up to 6 stories. The proposed project is 8 stories.
4)
Blank Walls – Per ODS Section 4.1.1, “Blank walls shall be limited to a maximum of twenty (20) 
feet in length on all stories”. The application includes a blank wall area exceeding 20 feet in length 
along the ﬁrst two ﬂoors of the building where parking and utility areas are provided.
5)
Massing Breaks – Per ODS Standard Section 4.4.7.A.3.b, the top of the building shall be 
diﬀerentiated from the base and the body by at least 2 of the following: building material, wall 
plane breaks (minimum of 2 feet in depth and 5 feet in length), stepback (minimum of 10 feet 
along all building facades), color, eaves, projected roof overhang (minimum of 18 inches), stepped 
parapets, or roof cornice/distinguishing architectural elements such as overhangs, pergolas, etc. 
on the uppermost ﬂoor). The applicant has partially met this standard by providing a deﬁned top 
along portions of the building, thought some portions of the top are not diﬀerentiated with at 
least 2 of the listed items as required.
6)
Façade Design – Per ODS Section 7.1.1.B, building façade design shall include a change in the 
street-fronting façade through the use of vertical recesses or projections, building height, and/or 
colors and materials at intervals of twenty-ﬁve (25) to ﬁfty (50)-feet. The project does not include 
the speciﬁed changes in street-fronting facades at the intervals speciﬁed.
7)
Setbacks – The proposed project is located within the Vision of the Gateway Speciﬁc Plan Area, 
which includes speciﬁc setback requirements that supersede those required for the zoning district 
in which the project is located.
i.
Per ODS Section 7.7.1.A.2, along the south side of Third Avenue, a minimum setback of 20 feet 
from the Third Avenue property line is required. The project has a setback of 3.1 feet along 
Third Avenue.
ii.
Per ODS Section 7.7.1.A.3, along neighborhood streets, a minimum setback between Fifteen
(15) to a maximum of twenty (20) feet from the property line is required. The project has 
setbacks of 2.5 feet along Eldorado St., and 9 feet along S Delaware St.
8)
Stepbacks – The proposed project is located within the Vision of the Gateway Speciﬁc Plan Area, 
which includes speciﬁc stepback requirements that supersede those required for the zoning

--- page 81 ---


--- page 82 ---
district in which the project is located.
i.
Per ODS Section 7.7.1.B.1, along the south side of Third Avenue, an additional 8-foot minimum 
stepback shall be provided along the right of way face for the portion of the building above 30 
feet in height. The project has identiﬁed a waiver for a reduced stepback along Third Avenue.
ii.
Per ODS Section 7.7.1.B.2, along neighborhood streets, an additional 8-foot minimum 
stepback shall be provided along the right of way face for the portion of the building above 25 
feet in height. The project proposes a waiver for reduced stepbacks along Eldorado St. and S 
Delaware St.
9)
Residential Entries – Per ODS Section 7.7.3.A.1, along the south Side of Third Avenue and along 
neighborhood streets, front door entries shall be located at intervals of at least every 25 to 30 
feet. Where residential entries to townhome units are proposed along Third Ave., they are 
provided with 28-foot spacing, in compliance with this standard. However, residential entries are 
not proposed at regular intervals along S Delaware St. or Eldorado St.
i.
Additionally, Per ODS Section 7.7.3.A.3.b, along the south side of Third Avenue, porches shall 
be allowed within the front setback area up to within 10 feet of the property line. The porches 
for four townhome units fronting Third Ave. are located less than 10 feet from the property 
line.
10) Ground Floor Residential Entries – Per ODS Section 4.2.1, entries to ground ﬂoor residential units 
shall be located 18 to 42 inches above or below the grade of the adjacent public sidewalk. The 
ground ﬂoor entries to four townhome units along Third Ave. are proposed from 10 to 21 inches 
above exterior grade.
11) Architectural Styles and Materials – Per ODS Section 7.7.1.D at least one of the following are 
required per unit on all street-facing facades (porches, bay windows, decorative walls up to a max. 
height of three feet, or window boxes). There are units provided that do not include one of the 
elements speciﬁed. The project has identiﬁed a waiver to this standard, and has proposed other 
architectural features, such as Juliet balconies and recessed balconies/terraces on units at upper 
levels

GENERAL NOTES
1.   THESE CONSTRUCTION DOCUMENTS SET MINIMUM STANDARDS.  THE DRAWINGS SHALL GOVERN
OVER GENERAL NOTES TO THE EXTENT SHOWN. DO NOT SCALE THE DRAWINGS, NOTED DIMENSIONS
GOVERN. ALL DIMENSIONS ARE TO FACE OF SHEATHING OR ROUGH OPENING UNLESS OTHERWISE
NOTED.
2.    ALL WORK PERFORMED, INCLUDING MATERIALS FURNISHED, WORKMANSHIP, MEANS AND METHODS
OF CONSTRUCTION SHALL CONFORM TO THE APPLICABLE AND LATEST REQUIREMENTS OF THE
NATIONAL, STATE AND LOCAL BUILDING CODES, ALL LOCAL AND STATE HANDICAP ACCESS AND USE
REGULATIONS, ANY FIRE DEPARTMENT REGULATIONS, UTILITY COMPANY REQUIREMENTS AND
LANDLORD'S RULES AND REGULATIONS, AND GENERAL CONDITIONS OF APPLICABLE
OWNER/CONTRACTOR AGREEMENT.
3.   BEFORE COMMENCING WORK, THE CONTRACTOR SHALL FILE ALL REQUIRED CERTIFICATES  OF
INSURANCE WITH THE OWNER, LANDLORD AND THE DEPARTMENT OF BUILDINGS, OBTAIN ALL REQUIRED
PERMITS, AND PAY ALL FEES REQUIRED BY THE GOVERNING AGENCIES. NAME JONES ARCHITECTURE
AND THEIR AGENTS AS ADDITIONAL INSURED.
4.   DRAWINGS INDICATE LOCATION, DIMENSIONS, REFERENCE, AND TYPICAL DETAIL FOR
CONSTRUCTION.  MINOR DETAILS NOT USUALLY SHOWN OR SPECIFIED, BUT NECESSARY FOR PROPER
CONSTRUCTION OF ANY PART OF THE WORK SHALL BE INCLUDED AS IF THEY WERE INDICATED IN THE
DRAWINGS. FOR CONDITIONS NOT ILLUSTRATED, NOTIFY  ARCHITECT FOR CLARIFICATION AND/OR
SIMILAR DETAIL.
5.   CONTRACTOR SHALL EMPLOY ADEQUATE NUMBER OF SKILLED WORKMEN WHO ARE THOROUGHLY
TRAINED AND EXPERIENCED IN THE NECESSARY CRAFTS AND WHO ARE COMPLETELY FAMILIAR WITH
THE SPECIFIED REQUIREMENTS AND THE METHODS NEEDED FOR PROPER PERFORMANCE OF THE
WORK.  ALL WORK SHALL BE PERFORMED BY DULY  LICENSED TRADESMEN AND AS REQUIRED BY STATE
AND LOCAL GOVERNMENTS FOR EACH APPLICABLE TRADE, (PLUMBING, ELECTRICAL, ETC), WHO SHALL
ARRANGE FOR AND OBTAIN REQUIRED INSPECTIONS AND SIGN OFFS.
6.  THESE DRAWINGS ARE DIVIDED INTO SECTIONS FOR CONVENIENCE ONLY. CONTRACTOR,
SUBCONTRACTORS, VENDORS AND MATERIAL SUPPLIERS SHALL REFER TO ALL RELEVANT SECTIONS IN
BIDDING AND PERFORMING THEIR WORK AND SHALL BE RESPONSIBLE FOR ALL ASPECTS OF THEIR
WORK REGARDLESS OF WHERE THE INFORMATION OCCURS ON THE DRAWINGS.
7.   CONTRACTOR SHALL BE RESPONSIBLE TO COORDINATE WORK OF ALL TRADES AND SHALL PROVIDE
ALL DIMENSIONS REQUIRED FOR OTHER TRADES. SUBCONTRACTORS SHALL BE RESPONSIBLE FOR
COORDINATION OF THEIR WORK WITH THE WORK OF OTHERS, AND SHALL VERIFY THAT ANY WORK
RELATING TO THEM WHICH MUST BE PROVIDED BY OTHERS, HAS BEEN COMPLETED AND IS ADEQUATE
PRIOR TO COMMENCING THEIR WORK.
8.  CONTRACTOR SHALL PROVIDE STRUCTURAL BACKING/BLOCKING FOR ALL WALL MOUNTED FIXTURES,
FINISHES AND EQUIPMENT, AND FOR ALL HANGING FIXTURES, BLINDS, ETC.
9.  CONTRACTOR SHALL INSTALL ALL MATERIALS AND EQUIPMENT AS PER MANUFACTURER'S WRITTEN
INSTRUCTIONS AND/OR RECOMMENDATIONS.
10.  CONTRACTOR SHALL AT ALL TIMES DURING THE COURSE OF THE CONTRACT KEEP THE ADJOINING
PREMISES, INCLUDING STREETS AND OTHER AREAS ASSIGNED TO, OR USED BY THE CONTRACTOR, FREE
FROM ACCUMULATIONS OF WASTE MATERIALS AND RUBBISH  CAUSED BY CONTRACTOR'S EMPLOYEES,
SUBCONTRACTORS OR THEIR WORK.

PROJECT DESCRIPTION
WAIVER SUMMARY
A NEW 8-STORY BUILDING WITH 5-STORIES OF MULTI-FAMILY RESIDENTIAL TYPE III-A STRUCTURE OVER 
A 3-STORIES TYPE I-A STRUCTURE WHICH INCLUDE PARKING, BUILDING AMENITIES, AND RESIDENTIAL 
UNITS. THE PROPOSED BUILDING IS APPROXIMATELY 165,634 SF AND WILL PROVIDE 128 RESIDENTIAL 
UNITS.
THE PROPOSED 8 STORY, 128-UNIT RESIDENTIAL BUILDING EMBODIES A REFINED BLEND OF SPANISH 
REVIVAL AND MEDITERRANEAN ARCHITECTURAL STYLES. THE PROPOSAL INCLUDES FOR-RENT UNITS 
AND ASSOCIATED AMENITIES; IT DOES NOT INCLUDE SUBDIVISIONS OF THE LOTS OR CONDOMINIUMS. 
THE BUILDING AND ITS SITE ARE DESIGNED IN ACCORDANCE WITH THE OBJECTIVE DESIGN STANDARDS 
AS WELL AS THE STANDARDS SET FORTH BY EACH OF THE SPECIFIC PLAN AREAS WHICH INCLUDE BUT 
ARE NOT LIMITED TO FAÇADE MODULATION, WINDOW/BALCONY ALIGNMENTS, LIGHT COLORED STUCCO 
FACADES, WEATHERED BRICK FACADES, VARIED ROOF LINES, AND SIMULATED RED TILE ROOFS AND 
PARAPETS. ADDITIONALLY, THE OBJECTIVE DESIGN STANDARDS FOR BOTH SPECIFIC PLAN AREAS 
PRESCRIBE 13 ARCHITECTURAL ELEMENTS, 7 OF WHICH ARE TO BE INCLUDED. THE PROPOSED 
PROJECT IMPLEMENTS MULTI-LEVEL ROOFS, ASYMMETRICAL MASSING, ARCHES, ORNAMENTAL 
DETAILS, MULTI-PANE WINDOWS, DECORATIVE TILES, ORNAMENTAL DETAILS, AND DEEP RECESSED 
OPENINGS AT THE GROUND STORY LOBBY. THE DETAILING AND MATERIALITY OUTLINED HERE OFFER A 
MODERN INTERPRETATION ON TRADITIONAL CRAFTSMANSHIP, ESTABLISHING A DIALOGUE WITH THE 
REGION’S ARCHITECTURAL HERITAGE AND CREATING A VIBRANT COMMUNITY HUB BY BLENDING 
CONTEMPORARY LIVING WITH CULTURAL RICHNESS TO FOSTER ENGAGEMENT AND ENRICH THE URBAN 
LANDSCAPE.

PARKING SUMMARY
FACADE DESIGN
OBJECTIVE DESIGN STANDARDS, SEC 7.1.1.B
BUILDING FAÇADE DESIGN SHALL INCLUDE A CHANGE IN THE STREET-FRONTING FAÇADE THROUGH THE 
USE OF VERTICAL RECESSES OR PROJECTIONS, BUILDING HEIGHT, AND/OR COLORS AND MATERIALS AT 
INTERVALS OF TWENTY-FIVE (25) TO FIFTY (50)-FEET.
MASSING BREAKS
OBJECTIVE DESIGN STANDARDS, SEC 4.1.7.A.3.B
B.  THE TOP SHALL BE DIFFERENTIATED FROM THE BASE AND BODY BY AT LEAST TWO (2) OF THE 
FOLLOWING: 
I. BUILDING MATERIAL
II. WALL PLANE BREAK (MINIMUM OF TWO [2] FEET IN DEPTH AND FIVE [5] FEET IN LENGTH)
III. STEPBACK (MINIMUM TEN [10] FEET ALONG ALL BUILDING FACADES)
IV. COLOR
V. EAVES
VI. PROJECTED ROOF OVERHANG (MINIMUM EIGHTEEN [18] INCHES)
VII. STEPPED PARAPETS
VIII. ROOF CORNICE OR DISTINGUISHING ARCHITECTURAL ELEMENT(S) SUCH AS OVERHANGS, 
PERGOLAS, ETC. ON THE UPPERMOST FLOOR
MASSING AND ARTICULATION
OBJECTIVE DESIGN STANDARDS, SEC 7.7.1.D
ARCHITECTURAL STYLES AND MATERIALS. BUILDINGS SHALL INCORPORATE AT LEAST ONE (1) OF THE 
FOLLOWING PER UNIT ON ALL STREET-FACING FACADES:
1. PORCH(ES)
2. BAY WINDOW(S)
3. DECORATIVE WALL(S) UP TO A MAXIMUM HEIGHT OF THREE (3) FEET
4. WINDOW BOX(ES)

LOADING BERTH REQUIREMENTS
SAN MATEO MUNICIPAL CODE, SEC. 27.64.390A
SCHEDULE OF LOADING REQUIREMENTS
REQUIRED: THE REQUIREMENTS FOR OFF-STREET LOADING BERTHS MAY BE MODIFIED BY ONE OF THE 
FOLLOWING MEANS:
(A) APPROVAL OF A SITE PLAN AND ARCHITECTURAL REVIEW (SPAR) BY THE ZONING ADMINISTRATOR, 
BASED ON THE FOLLOWING FINDINGS:
(1) ADEQUATE ON-STREET PARKING IS AVAILABLE ALONG A PARCEL FRONTAGE TO ACCOMMODATE 
A LOADING BERTH;
(2) THE ON-STREET PARKING INTENDED FOR TEMPORARY LOADING PURPOSES IS LOCATED AT 
LEAST 50 FEET FROM ANY INTERSECTIONS, AND PROVIDES CONVENIENT ACCESS TO BUILDING 
ENTRANCES; AND
(3) THE STREET WIDTH IS ADEQUATE TO ACCOMMODATE LOADING VEHICLES WITHOUT IMPEDING 
USE OF THE SIDEWALK OR LOCAL TRAFFIC CIRCULATION OR OTHERWISE BE DETRIMENTAL TO 
PUBLIC SAFETY; OR
(B) APPROVAL OF A VARIANCE APPLICATION IN ACCORDANCE WITH CHAPTER 27.78.
TURNING RADII
SAN MATEO MUNICIPAL CODE, SEC. 27.64.130
27.64.130 TURNING RADII AND TURNAROUND REQUIREMENTS.
REQUIRED: (E) TURNING AISLES OR RAMPS WITH TWO-WAY TRAFFIC SHALL HAVE RADII AND AISLE 
WIDTHS SUFFICIENT FOR TWO (2) AUTOMOBILES TO PASS ON THE TURN. RAMP WIDTHS ON TURNS SHALL 
BE AS FOLLOWS:
MINIMUM TWO-WAY RAMP WIDTH
CURB TO CURB:   24′
WALL TO WALL:    28′
MINIMUM TWO-WAY RADIUS
TO INSIDE WALL: 16'
TO INSIDE CURB: 18'
PROPOSED: THE DIMENSIONS OF THE PROPOSED TWO-WAY TRAFFIC RAMP ARE FEASIBLE BASED ON 
VEHICLE TURN STUDIES SHOWING THAT PASSENGER VEHICLES AT SLOW SPEEDS COMMON INSIDE A 
GARAGE CAN SAFELY  MANEUVER. INCREASING THE SIZE OF THE PROPOSED RAMP WOULD REQUIRE A 
LARGER GARAGE AND WOULD RESULT IN THE LOSS OF ALL OF THE GROUND STORY TOWNHOME UNITS. 
MASSING BREAKS
OBJECTIVE DESIGN STANDARDS, SEC 4.1.7.B.2
2. VERTICAL WALL PLANE BREAKS. ARTICULATION SHALL BE PROVIDED ON ALL BUILDING FACADES. THIS 
SHALL BE
ACCOMPLISHED BY INCORPORATING AT LEAST THREE (3) OF THE FOLLOWING:
A. ROOF CORNICE ON THE TOP FLOOR
B. A STEPBACK OR PROJECTION OF A MINIMUM OF FIVE (5) FEET IN DEPTH BETWEEN THE BASE AND THE
BODY OF THE BUILDING, MEANING THE BODY CAN BE RECESSED OR PROJECTED RELATIVE TO THE BASE.
ALONG THE PRIMARY AND SECONDARY FRONTAGES, PROJECTIONS FROM THE BASE SHALL ONLY OCCUR 
ON THE
BODY OF THE BUILDING. NO WALL PLANE SHALL EXTEND INTO THE REQUIRED SETBACK OR PUBLIC 
RIGHT-OFWAY.
C. CHANGE IN BUILDING MATERIAL OR COLOR BETWEEN THE BASE AND BODY CHARACTERIZED BY A 
MINIMUM
TWELVE (12)-INCH OFFSET FROM THE SURROUNDING BUILDING WALL
D. A STEPBACK OF A MINIMUM TEN (10)-FEET IMMEDIATELY ABOVE THE BUILDING BASE OR FOR THE TOP
FLOOR

7
GROUND STORY PLAN - RESIDENTIAL ENTRIES DIAGRAM
BUILDING HEIGHT
SETBACKS
RESIDENTIAL ENTRIES
GROUND FLOOR
STEPBACKS
OBJECTIVE DESIGN STANDARDS, SEC 4.2.1
GROUND FLOOR REQUIREMENTS: RESIDENTIAL
REQUIRED: ENTRIES TO GROUND-FLOOR RESIDENTIAL UNITS SHALL BE LOCATED EIGHTEEN (18) TO FORTY-TWO (42) INCHES ABOVE OR BELOW THE GRADE OF THE ADJACENT PUBLIC SIDEWALK. 
PROPOSED: UNITS ENTRIES RANGE FROM 10" - 21" ABOVE EXTERIOR GRADE. ANY ADDITIONAL HEIGHT AT THE ENTRIES WOULD CREATE HEAD CLEARANCE RESTRICTIONS AT THE ACCESSIBLE CORRIDOR AND UNITS. 
ADDITIONALLY, LOCATING THE UNIT ENTRIES 18" - 42" BELOW EXTERIOR GRADE WOULD CREATE CLEARANCE RESTRICTIONS AT THE UNDERGROUND PARKING LEVEL. 
3 IMPACTED UNITS 
2040 GENERAL PLAN, CHAPTER 2: TABLE LU-1 LAND USE DESIGNATIONS
DESIGNATION: MIXED USE MEDIUM II
REQUIRED: 4-6 STORIES 
NET LOSS OF 39 UNITS ON 7TH & 8TH STORIES
21 UNITS ON 7TH STORY; 18 UNITS ON 8TH STORY
PROPOSED: 8 STORIES
OBJECTIVE DESIGN STANDARDS, SEC 7.7.1.B.1 & 7.7.1.B.2
MASSING & ARTICULATION: STEPBACKS
REQUIRED: 7.7.1.B.2 ALONG NEIGHBORHOOD STREETS: ABOVE TWENTY-FIVE (25) FEET BUILDING HEIGHT, AN ADDITIONAL EIGHT (8)-FOOT MINIMUM STEPBACK SHALL BE PROVIDED ALONG THE RIGHT-OF-WAY FACADE  
PROPOSED : THE BUILDING FEATURES VARIED MASSING WITH PORTIONS STEPPING BACK ABOVE THE SECOND STORY AND OTHERS EXTENDING CLOSER TO THE RIGHT-OF-WAY (ROW). THIS MODULATION MAXIMIZES 
THE DENSITY BONUS ALLOWED UNDER SB330 WHILE MAINTAINING ADAQUATE CLEARANCES ALONG DELAWARE FROM THE OVERHEAD POWER LINES. THE ELDORADO FRONTAGE, AS A RESULT OF THE POWERLINE 
CLEARANCES, IS REQUIRED TO BE AS SHONW IN ORDER TO PROVIDE ADEQUATE SQUARE FOOTAGE FOR THE THREE UNITS AT EACH STORY OF THE BUILDING.
23 UNITS IMPACTED
OBJECTIVE DESIGN STANDARDS, SEC 7.7.3.2.B & 7.7.3.3A
WINDOWS, DOORS, AND ENTRY DESIGN: RESIDENTIAL ENTRIES
REQUIRED: 2.B. ON NEIGHBORHOOD STREETS OPEN PORCHES MAY EXTEND INTO THE FRONT SETBACK AREA UP TO WITHIN TEN (10) FEET OF THE PROPERTY LINE.
3.A. ALONG THE SOUTH SIDE OF THIRD AVENUE AND ALL OF FOURTH AVENUE PORCHES SHALL BE ALLOWED WITHIN THE FRONT SETBACK AREA UP TO WITHIN TEN (10) FEET OF THE PROPERTY LINE. 
PROPOSED : PORCHES PROVIDE A BUFFER AND PRIVACY TO BEDROOMS LOCATED DIRECTLY BEHIND. LOCATING PORCHES PER THE ODS (10' FROM THE PL) LIMITS THE DEPTH AND VIABILITY OF THE GROUND STORY 
UNITS. 
4 UNITS IMPACTED
OBJECTIVE DESIGN STANDARDS, SEC 7.7.1.A.2 & 7.7.1.A.3
MASSING & ARTICULATION: SETBACKS
REQUIRED: THE FOLLOWING SETBACKS SHALL SUPERSEDE THOSE REQUIRED FOR THE ZONING DISTRICT IN WHICH THE PROJECT IS LOCATED:
A.2. ALONG THE SOUTH SIDE OF THIRD AVENUE AND ALL OF FOURTH AVENUE: FIFTEEN (15) TO TWENTY (20) FEET FROM THE PROPERTY LINE 
A.3. ALONG NEIGHBORHOOD STREETS: FIFTEEN (15) TO TWENTY (20) FEET FROM THE PROPERTY LINE 
PROPOSED: PROVIDING THE REQUIRED SETBACKS ON THE GROUND STORY WOULD IMPACT THE VIABILITY OF THE UNITS BY REDUCING THEIR DEPTH TO AN UNOCCUPIABLE SIZE. FURTHERMORE, A SETBACK ON THE 
GROUND STORY INCREASES THE STEPBACK REQUIRED ON THE UPPER LEVELS FURTHER LIMITING THE PROJECT'S ABITILITY TO PROVIDE ADEQUATELY DEEP UNITS AND TO MEET THE ALLOWED UNIT DENSITY PER 
DENSITY BONUS LAW.
4 UNITS IMPACTED
PROPOSED:   
AREA WITHIN MIN SETBACK
   
AREA BEYOND MAX SETBACK 
  
(UTILIZED FOR PUBLIC ACCESSIBLE OPEN SPACE)
OBJECTIVE DESIGN STANDARDS, SEC 7.7.1.B.1 & 7.7.1.B.2
MASSING & ARTICULATION: STEPBACKS
REQUIRED: 7.71.B.1 ALONG THE SOUTH SIDE OF THIRD AVENUE AND ALL OF FOURTH AVENUE: ABOVE THIRTY (30) FEET OF BUILDING HEIGHT, AN ADDITIONAL EIGHT (8)-FOOT MINIMUM STEPBACK SHALL BE PROVIDED 
ALONG THE RIGHT-OF-WAY FACADE 
PROPOSED : THE BUILDING FEATURES VARIED MASSING WITH PORTIONS STEPPING BACK ABOVE THE SECOND STORY. THE STEPBACKS PROVIDED ALONG 3RD AVENUE ALLOW FOR THE MAXIMUM NUMBER OF UNITS 
ALLOWED BY DENSITY BONUS LAW. FURTHER REDUCING THE DEPTH OF THE UNITS WITH GREATER SETBACKS IMPACTS THE VIABILITY OF THE DWELLING UNITS DUE TO THE SHALLOW UNIT DEPTH
34 UNITS IMPACTED
BLANK WALLS
OBJECTIVE DESIGN STANDARDS, SEC 4.1.1
MASSING & ARTICULATION: BLANK WALLS
REQUIRED: BLANK WALLS SHALL BE LIMITED TO A MAXIMUM OF TWENTY (20) FEET IN LENGTH ON ALL STORIES. 
BLANK WALL: A GROUND-FLOOR WALL OR PORTION OF A GROUND-FLOOR WALL OVER TEN (10) FEET IN HEIGHT AND A HORIZONTAL LENGTH GREATER THAN TWENTY (20) FEET AND DOES NOT INCLUDE A TRANSPARENT 
WINDOW OR DOOR.
PROPOSED: UTILITIES ARE GROUPED ON STREET FRONTAGE PER PG&E REQUIREMENTS

FACADE DESIGN
OBJECTIVE DESIGN STANDARDS, SEC. 7.1.1.B
REQUIRED: BUILDING FAÇADE DESIGN SHALL INCLUDE A CHANGE IN THE STREET-FRONTING FAÇADE THROUGH THE USE OF VERTICAL RECESSES OR PROJECTIONS, BUILDING HEIGHT, AND/OR COLORS AND 
MATERIALS AT INTERVALS OF TWENTY-FIVE (25) TO FIFTY (50)-FEET.
PROPOSED: FURTHER MODULATING THE FACADE PUSHES THE HIGHLIGHTED STACK OF UNITS FURTHER INTO THE BUILDING. BECAUSE OF THE NARROW 'L' SHAPED SITE, SHIFTING UNITS INTO THE BUILDING PUSHES 
THE UNITS TOO CLOSE TO THE SHARED PROPERTY LINE (SEE PLAN DIMENSION CALLOUT) TO ALLOW ADEQUATE OPENINGS PER CBC TABLE 705.8. THE DESIGN ACHIEVES THE INTENT OF THE OBJECTIVE STANDARD 
WITH THE RECESSED BALCONIES AT THE REQUIRED INTERVALS. A WAIVER IS PREEMPTIVELY REQUESTED TO ADDRESS FEEDBACK FROM PLANNERS TO FURTHER MODULATE THE FACADE.

1/32" = 1'-0"

LEVEL 04 FLOOR PLAN
OBJECTIVE DESIGN STANDARDS, SEC. 7.7.1.D
REQUIRED:
ARCHITECTURAL STYLES AND MATERIALS. BUILDINGS SHALL INCORPORATE AT LEAST ONE (1) OF THE FOLLOWING PER UNIT ON ALL STREET-FACING FACADES:
1. PORCH(ES)
2. BAY WINDOW(S)
3. DECORATIVE WALL(S) UP TO A MAXIMUM HEIGHT OF THREE (3) FEET
4. WINDOW BOX(ES)
PROPOSED: THE PROJECT IS DESIGNED IN THE SPANISH REVIVAL/CALIFORNIA MEDITERRANEAN STYLE, WITH CONSISTENT DETAILING ACROSS ALL FAÇADES. DUE TO THE SITE'S LOCATION WITHIN OVERLAPPING 
SPECIFIC PLAN AREAS, SOME RESIDENTIAL-SCALE DESIGN REQUIREMENTS FROM SECTION 7.7.1.D OF THE THE VISION OF THE GATEWAY PLAN AREA ARE NOT APPROPRIATE FOR A BUILDING SIZED FOR THE 
DOWNTOWN SPECIFIC PLAN. THEREFORE, THE DESIGN TEAM REQUESTS A WAIVER OF SECTION 7.7.1.D. DESPITE THIS, THE DESIGN IMPLEMENTS DETAILS THAT WE FEEL MEET THE INTENT OF BOTH PLAN AREAS, 
SPECIFICALLY 7.7.1.D, BY INCORPORATING:
•4 PORCHES AT TOWNHOMES
•72 RECESSED BALCONIES/TERRACES FOR UPPER-LEVEL UNITS
•52 JULIET BALCONIES AT URBAN 1-BED UNITS
THE RECESSED BALCONIES MEET THE INTENT FOR PORCHES AND JULIET RAILINGS MEET THE INTENT FOR DECORATIVE PARTIAL HEIGHT WALLS. NEITHER A PORCH, OR PARTIAL HEIGHT WALL IS FEASIBLE AT UPPER 
LEVEL UNITS. ADDITIONALLY, IN RESPONSE TO SECTIONS 7.1.2.A & 7.7.2.A, WE NOTE THAT REQUIRING EACH UNIT TO HAVE A BAY WINDOW OF A DIFFERENT MATERIAL WOULD RESULT IN AN EXCESSIVE USE OF ACCENT 
MATERIALS, CONFLICTING WITH THE INTENDED DESIGN HIERARCHY. FINALLY, WINDOW BOXES—WHICH ARE NOT CLEARLY DEFINED IN CHAPTER 8 BUT ASSUMED TO MEAN WINDOW PLANTER BOXES—WHICH WOULD BE 
LOCATED AT THE FLOOR LINE WHERE THE WINDOW SILL IS LOCATED, ARE IMPRACTICAL AND UNSAFE AT UPPER LEVELS, POSE MAINTENANCE CHALLENGES FOR PROPERTY MANAGERS, AND ARE UNLIKELY TO BE 
PROPERLY MAINTAINED BY RESIDENTS. WE BELIEVE THE PROPOSED DESIGN MEETS THE SPIRIT AND INTENT OF THE APPLICABLE GUIDELINES, WHILE ADDRESSING SCALE, FEASIBILITY, AND LONG-TERM MAINTENANCE.

OBJECTIVE DESIGN STANDARDS, SEC. 4.1.7.A.3.b
REQUIRED:
B.  THE TOP SHALL BE DIFFERENTIATED FROM THE BASE AND BODY BY AT LEAST TWO (2) OF THE FOLLOWING: 
I. BUILDING MATERIAL
II. WALL PLANE BREAK (MINIMUM OF TWO [2] FEET IN DEPTH AND FIVE [5] FEET IN LENGTH)
III. STEPBACK (MINIMUM TEN [10] FEET ALONG ALL BUILDING FACADES)
IV. COLOR
V. EAVES
VI. PROJECTED ROOF OVERHANG (MINIMUM EIGHTEEN [18] INCHES)
VII. STEPPED PARAPETS
VIII. ROOF CORNICE OR DISTINGUISHING ARCHITECTURAL ELEMENT(S) SUCH AS OVERHANGS, PERGOLAS, ETC. ON THE UPPERMOST FLOOR
PROPOSED: THE PROJECT TEAM HAS RESPONDED TO DIRECT FEEDBACK FROM STAFF AND FROM THE PUBLIC FROM THE TIME OF THE INITIAL SUBMITTAL THROUGH THIS RESUBMITTAL. AT THE 8TH STORY, THE 
BUILDING DESIGN PROPOSES AT LEAST TWO OF THE FOLLOWING ON EACH FAÇADE:
•BUILDING MATERIAL SHIFT
•A WALL PLANE BREAK (2FT IN DEPTH, 5FT IN WIDTH)
•A STEPBACK (AT LEAST 10FT)
•PROJECTED ROOF OVERHANG (MINIMUM OF 18 IN)
•ROOF CORNICE OR DISTINGUISHING ARCHITECTURAL ELEMENT SUCH AS OVERHANGS, PERGOLAS, ETC. ON THE UPPERMOST FLOORS.
ADDITIONALLY, THE PROPOSED BUILDING MASS DIRECTLY ADDRESSES TWO STANDARDS OUTLINED IN THE SPECIFIC PLAN AREAS WHICH THIS SITE IS LOCATED WITHIN. 7.1.2.B & 7.7.2.B PRESCRIBE THAT STRUCTURES 
SHALL INCLUDE 7 OF 13 DESIGN ELEMENTS, TWO OF WHICH ARE MULTI-LEVEL ROOFS AND ASYMMETRICAL MASSING. THE DESIGN ADDRESSES THE INTENT OF THIS STANDARD ON ALL FACADES AS WELL AS 
ADDRESSES THE STANDARDS OF THE SPECIFIC PLAN AREAS WHICH ACCORDING TO 2.2.D SUPERSEDE CITY-WIDE REQUIREMENTS. THIS WAIVER IS REQUESTED PREEMPTIVELY TO ADDRESS FEEDBACK FROM 
PLANNERS BOTH VERBALLY AND IN THE ODS RESPONSES ISSUED FOLLOWING THE FORMAL SUBMITTAL IN MARCH.
LOADING BERTH REQUIREMENTS
SAN MATEO MUNICIPAL CODE, SEC. 27.64.390A
SCHEDULE OF LOADING REQUIREMENTS
REQUIRED: THE REQUIREMENTS FOR OFF-STREET LOADING BERTHS MAY BE MODIFIED BY ONE OF THE FOLLOWING MEANS:
(A) APPROVAL OF A SITE PLAN AND ARCHITECTURAL REVIEW (SPAR) BY THE ZONING ADMINISTRATOR, BASED ON THE FOLLOWING FINDINGS:
(1) ADEQUATE ON-STREET PARKING IS AVAILABLE ALONG A PARCEL FRONTAGE TO ACCOMMODATE A LOADING BERTH;
(2) THE ON-STREET PARKING INTENDED FOR TEMPORARY LOADING PURPOSES IS LOCATED AT LEAST 50 FEET FROM ANY INTERSECTIONS, AND PROVIDES CONVENIENT ACCESS TO BUILDING ENTRANCES; AND
(3) THE STREET WIDTH IS ADEQUATE TO ACCOMMODATE LOADING VEHICLES WITHOUT IMPEDING USE OF THE SIDEWALK OR LOCAL TRAFFIC CIRCULATION OR OTHERWISE BE DETRIMENTAL TO PUBLIC SAFETY; OR
(B) APPROVAL OF A VARIANCE APPLICATION IN ACCORDANCE WITH CHAPTER 27.78.
PROPOSED: DUE TO A DRIVE ENTRY BEING PROHIBITED OFF OF 3RD AVE OR DELAWARE ST, AND DUE TO THE NATURE OF THE SITE AND THE NARROW WIDTH FROM THE 3RD AVE CURB TO THE PROPERY LINE, WE ARE LIMITED 
TO THE CURRENT PARKING ENTRY LOCATION AND LOADING ZONE LOCATION ON ELDORADO ST. THE CURRENT PARKING ENTRY LOCATION DOES NOT ALLOW THE 50' REQUIRED DISTANCE FROM THE PROPOSED LOADING ZONE 
AND TRASH STAGING AREA TO THE INTERSECTION AT 3RD AND ELDORADO ST.

SAN MATEO MUNICIPAL CODE, SEC. 27.64.130
27.64.130 TURNING RADII AND TURNAROUND REQUIREMENTS.
REQUIRED: (E) TURNING AISLES OR RAMPS WITH TWO-WAY TRAFFIC SHALL HAVE RADII AND AISLE WIDTHS SUFFICIENT FOR TWO (2) AUTOMOBILES TO PASS ON THE TURN. RAMP WIDTHS ON TURNS SHALL BE AS FOLLOWS:
MINIMUM TWO-WAY RAMP WIDTH
CURB TO CURB:   24′
WALL TO WALL:    28′
MINIMUM TWO-WAY RADIUS
TO INSIDE WALL: 16'
TO INSIDE CURB: 18'
PROPOSED: THE DIMENSIONS OF THE PROPOSED TWO-WAY TRAFFIC RAMP ARE FEASIBLE BASED ON VEHICLE TURN STUDIES SHOWING THAT PASSENGER VEHICLES AT SLOW SPEEDS COMMON INSIDE A GARAGE CAN SAFELY  
MANEUVER. INCREASING THE SIZE OF THE PROPOSED RAMP WOULD REQUIRE A LARGER GARAGE AND WOULD RESULT IN THE LOSS OF ALL OF THE GROUND STORY TOWNHOME UNITS.

NAME

6
5
20
INTERIOR FINISHES AND AMENITIES OF AFFORDABLE UNITS WILL EQUAL TO 
THAT OF THE MARKET RATE UNITS.
AFFORDABLE UNITS WILL HAVE THE SAME ACCESS AND ENJOYMENT OF 
COMMON SPACE, PARKING, STORAGE, AND OTHER FACILITIES IN THE 
RESIDENTIAL PROJECT.
THE PROJECT IS LOCATED WITHIN THE MIXED USE MEDIUM II LAND USE 
DISTRICT OF THE SAN MATEO GENERAL PLAN, WHICH ALLOWS A MAXIMUM OF 
99 DU/AC, AND WHICH EQUATES TO A MAXIMUM RESIDENTIAL DENSITY OF 64 
UNITS ON THE PROJECT SITE. THE PROJECT IMPLEMENTS THE DBL TO 
INCLUDE 15% VERY LOW INCOME UNITS (10 UNITS) TO RECEIVE A 50% 
DENSITY BONUS (32 UNITS), AND FURTHER PROVIDES 15% MODERATE UNITS 
(10 UNITS) TO RECEIVE AN ADDITIONAL 50% DENSITY BONUS (32 UNITS), 
WHICH EQUATES TO A TOTAL UNIT COUNT OF 128 UNITS. (GOV. CODE § 
65915(F)(2))

PROPERTYLINE
PROPERTYLINE
PROPERTYLINE
PROPERTYLINE
DESIGN-BUILD IRRIGATION SHALL MEET THE FOLLOWING REQUIREMENTS
1.
ALL LANDSCAPE AREAS WILL BE PERMANENTLY IRRIGATED USING A FULLY
AUTOMATIC IRRIGATION SYSTEM.
2.
SYSTEM WILL BE  100%SUB-SURFACE DRIP IRRIGATION WITH A
COMBINATION OF DRIP EMITTERS AND EMITTER RINGS.
3.
ALL IRRIGATION IMPROVEMENTS WILL UTILIZE HIGH EFFICIENCY DESIGN
AND EQUIPMENT COMPONENTS IN CONFORMANCE WITH CITY OF SAN
MATEO STANDARDS AND REQUIREMENTS.
4.
THE IRRIGATION SYSTEM DESIGN WILL COMPLY WITH ABA  1881
REQUIREMENTS .FOLLOW THE STATEWIDE MODEL ORDINANCE GUIDELINE
AND CITY REQUIREMENTS WITH THE USE OF WATER-EFFICIENCY
LANDSCAPE AND LOW WATER USE PLANTS.
5.
IRRIGATION SYSTEM PLANS AND DESIGN WILL BE PROVIDED AT A LATER
DATE
6.
INSTALL WEATHER BASED IRRIGATION TIMER AND FLOW SENSOR.
SPECIFIED CONTROLLER NEEDS A MONTHLY FEE TO BE ACTIVE. CONSIDER
A WEATHER BASED CONTROLLER THAT EITHER COLLECTS WEATHER DATA
ON SITE OR IS CONNECTED TO INTERNET TO COLLECT WEATHER DATA.
7.
IRRIGATION CONTROLLERS SHALL BE OF A TYPE WHICH DOES NOT LOSE
8.
PROGRAMMING DATA IN THE EVENT THE PRIMARY POWER SOURCE IS
INTERRUPTED.
9.
PRESSURE REGULATORS SHALL BE INSTALLED ON THE IRRIGATION
SYSTEM TO ENSURE THE DYNAMIC PRESSURE OF THE SYSTEM IS WITHIN
THE MANUFACTURERS RECOMMENDED PRESSURE RANGE.
10. MANUAL SHUT-OFF VALVES (SUCH AS A GATE VALVE ,BALL VALVE ,OR
BUTTERFLY VALVE )SHALL BE INSTALLED AS CLOSE AS POSSIBLE TO THE
POINT OF CONNECTION OF THE WATER SUPPLY.
11. ALL IRRIGATION EMITTER DEVICES MUST MEET THE REQUIREMENTS SET IN
THE ANSI STANDARD ,ASABE/ICC " .802-2014LANDSCAPE IRRIGATION
SPRINKLER AND EMITTER STANDARD ",ALL SPRINKLER HEADS INSTALLED
IN THE LANDSCAPE MUST DOCUMENT A DISTRIBUTION UNIFORMITY LOW
QUARTER OF  0.65OR HIGHER USING THE PROTOCOL DEFINED IN
ASABE/ICC .802-2014
12. AREAS LESS THAN TEN FEET IN WIDTH IN ANY DIRECTION SHALL BE
IRRIGATED WITH SUBSURFACE IRRIGATION OR OTHER MEANS THAT
PRODUCES NO RUNOFF OR OVERSPRAY
13. ONCE ENTIRE LANDSCAPE IS INSTALLED CONTACT MID-PENINSULA
WATER DISTRICT TO SCHEDULE A FINAL WELO INSPECTION. WELO REPORT
GENERATED FROM INSPECTION NEEDS TO BE TURNED IN TO MPWD TO BE
SIGNED OFF PRIOR TO CLOSING BUILDING PERMIT.
14. A CERTIFICATE OF COMPLETION WILL NEED TO BE TURNED IN TO MPWD
WITH FINAL WELO REPORT TO BE SIGNED OFF PRIOR TO CLOSING
BUILDING PERMIT.
