RE: 
PA24-065 620 Full Application Submittal - 668 E. 3rd Ave.  
 
Dear Mr. Dahl, 
 
Prometheus Real Estate Group respectfully and formally submits this Project Description Letter and 
associated materials for the full development application associated with the Project proposal located 
at 668 E. 3rd Avenue - PA24-065 620. 
 
The Project’s pre-application was submitted pursuant to SB 330, which amended the Housing 
Accountability Act (Gov. Code § 65889.5), the Permit Streamlining Act (Gov. Code § 65920 et seq.), and 
created the Housing Crisis Act of 2019 (Gov. Code § 66300).  This full application is timely submitted to 
preserve the vesting secured by the pre-application. 
 
The Project application is consistent with the guidelines of the adopted San Mateo General Plan 2040 in 
proposing a 128-unit residential development. It will allow an aging strip retail center and parking lot to 
convert to much needed market rate and affordable rental housing within walking distance to 
Downtown San Mateo and Caltrain and is consistent with the policies and guidelines of the San Mateo 
General Plan. 
 
We believe that this request is fully consistent with San Mateo’s vision and goals of providing housing 
opportunities in focused areas of San Mateo as guided by the recently adopted General Plan. This 0.64-
acre site is situated within the Mixed Use Medium II designation of the General Plan in downtown San 
Mateo.1 This proposal supports guiding language of the San Mateo General Plan to “Encourage new 
development to maximize the density and intensity specified in the Land Use Plan and to efficiently use 
land and infrastructure resources” and ”provide a range of housing types, sizes, and affordability levels in 
all San Mateo neighborhoods” (Policy LU 1.3).” Accompanying this Project Description Letter are the 
required Project plans and application documents. 
 
I. 
Project Description 
 
The Project will consist of eight stories of residential units comprised of studio, one-bedroom, two- 
bedroom, and three-bedroom units over an internal and underground parking garage, the entrance of 
which will be visually minimized per Policy CD 7.4. Amenity spaces on ground floor, second floor, and 
the 8th floor will provide gathering space for the residents.    
 
In keeping with Policy CD 7.3, the Project design enhances the neighborhood’s visual and architectural 
 
1 
The Project complies with the General Plan’s base density of 99 units per acre and therefore should be 
processed by the Zoning Administrator pursuant to Municipal Code section 27.06.020(h).

--- page 157 ---
character by providing high-quality materials and construction, open space, and resident amenities. 
The proposed 8 story, 128-unit residential building embodies a refined blend of Spanish Revival and 
Mediterranean architectural styles that are integral to both the Downtown specific plan area and the 
Vision of the Gateway specific plan area outlined in the Objective Design Standards. Furthermore, the 
proposed Project is designed in accordance the standards set forth by each of the specific plan areas 
which include but are not limited to façade modulation, window/balcony alignments, light colored 
stucco facades, weathered brick facades, varied roof lines, and simulated red tile roofs and parapets. 
Additionally, the objective design standards for both specific plan areas prescribe 13 architectural 
elements, 7 of which are to be included. The proposed Project implements multi-level roofs, 
asymmetrical massing, arches, ornamental details, multi pane windows, decorative tiles, ornamental 
details, and deep recessed openings at the ground story lobby. The proposed design is a modern 
interpretation on the Spanish Revival and Mediterranean styles, establishing a dialogue with the 
region’s architectural heritage and creating a vibrant community hub by blending contemporary living 
with cultural richness to foster engagement and enrich the urban landscape. 
 
II. 
Density Bonus Law 
 
The Project incorporates the use of the State Density Bonus Law (Gov. Code § 65915 [“DBL”]). The DBL 
has four distinct primary components: (1) Density Bonuses; (2) Incentives; (3) Development Standard 
Waivers; and (4) Parking Standard Waivers. Although interrelated, each component serves a different 
purpose and is governed by unique standards.  
A. 
Density Bonus 
 
Section 65915(b)(1) of the DBL provides that requests for a density bonus must be granted “when an 
applicant for a housing development seeks and agrees to construct a housing development” that meets 
one or more of the statute’s thresholds, including at least 5% of the units for very low income 
households. 
 
The Project is located within the Mixed Use Medium II land use district of the San Mateo General Plan, 
which allows a maximum of 99 du/ac, and which equates to a maximum residential density of 64 units 
on the Project site. The Project implements the DBL to include 15% Very Low Income units (10 Units) to 
receive a 50% density bonus (32 units), and further provides 15% Moderate units (10 Units) to receive an 
additional 50% density bonus (32 Units), which equates to a total unit count of 128 units. (Gov. Code § 
65915(f)(2).   
 
B. 
Incentives 
A local agency must grant an incentive request unless it can make a written finding, based on substantial 
evidence, that: (1) the incentive does not result in identifiable and actual cost reductions to provide for 
affordable housing costs; (2) the incentive would have a specific, adverse impact on the public health or 
safety, or upon an historical resource; or (3) would be contrary to state or federal law. (Gov. Code 
§ 65915(d)(1).) We submit that none of those findings can be made with regard to this Project. 
Recent case law confirms that an applicant is not required to establish that the requested incentive will 
result in cost reductions. In Schreiber v. City of Los Angeles (2021) 69 Cal.App.5th 549, 555, the court 
explained that there is a presumption that an incentive will result in cost reductions and that an 
applicant “is not required to establish that cost reductions will result.” Instead, a city must approve the 
incentive request unless it makes one of the written findings set forth in Section 65915(d)(1) above.

--- page 158 ---
(Ibid.) “By requiring the city to grant incentives unless it makes particular findings, the statute places the 
burden of proof on the city to overcome the presumption that incentives will result in cost reductions.” 
(Id. at 556.) Because of this presumption, a city is “not required to make an affirmative finding that the 
incentives would result in cost reductions, or to cite evidence to establish a fact presumed to be true.” 
(Id. at 560.) 
 
The number of incentives is derived from the amount of affordable units that are provided. In this case, 
by providing at least 15% of the units for VLI households, the Project applicant may receive three 
incentives. (§ 65915(d)(2)(C).) This Project Application does not identify the use of any Incentives at 
this time.   
However, we reserve our right to identify and seek the three incentives available in response to feedback 
from City staff during the entitlement process. 
 
C. 
Development Standard Waivers 
 
In addition to, and separate from, requests for incentives, a DBL applicant may request a waiver or 
reduction of development standards that would have the effect of physically precluding the construction 
of the Project proposed by the developer. (Gov. Code § 65915(e)(1).) The definition of a “development 
standard” includes a site or construction condition, including, without limitation, local height, setback, 
floor area ratio, onsite open space, and parking area ratio requirements that would otherwise apply to 
residential development pursuant to ordinances, general plan elements, specific plans, charters, or 
other local condition, law, policy, resolution, or regulation. (Gov. Code § 65915(o)(1).) A request for a 
development standard waiver neither reduces nor increases the number of incentives to which the 
developer is otherwise entitled. (Gov. Code § 65915(e)(2).) Furthermore, there is no limit on the 
number of waivers that may be issued. 
As with incentives, recent case law has clarified the legal principles regarding waivers. The Schreiber 
case confirms that a city may refuse a request to waive or reduce development standards only if it 
makes written findings that the waiver or reduction would have a specific adverse impact on the public 
health or safety. (Id. at 556; Gov. Code § 65915(e)(1).) In addition, another new case upholding a city’s 
approval of a DBL Project confirmed that waivers are based on the Project as proposed by the 
developer: “even if we assume the Project as designed is inconsistent with some of the City’s design 
standards, the Density Bonus Law would preclude the City from applying those standards to deny this 
Project.” (Bankers Hill 150 v. City of San Diego (2022) 74 Cal.App.5th 755, 775.) Therefore, a local agency 
may not respond to a waiver request that a Project could be redesigned to avoid the need for a waiver. 
(Id. at 774-775 [rejecting argument that the Project “could have been built more horizontally” to comply 
with design standards.”].)  In addition, HCD has notified various local agencies that they cannot require a 
qualifying DBL Project to be redesigned in order to avoid the need for a waiver.  Last year, HCD advised 
the City of Oceanside as follows: “HCD reminds the City that appellate courts have established (and 
continue to affirm) that local agencies cannot lawfully redesign a qualifying SDBL Project on the theory 
that if the Project were configured differently, it would not need the requested incentives/concessions 
and waivers. (Wollmer v. City of Berkeley (2011) 193 Cal.App.4th 1329, 1346–1347.)  The City must 
consider the Project as proposed, inclusive of any requested concessions or waivers.”2   
 
At this point, we identify the following waivers or reductions to the development standards identified 
below (As identified on page G002 of the Plan Set and below):

D. 
Parking Standard Waivers and AB 2097 
 
Parking ratio reductions are separate from the incentives and waivers identified above. By providing 
more than 11% VLI units, the Project may request a cap of 0.5 spaces per unit because the Project is 
within a half mile of a major transit stop with unobstructed access. (Gov. Code § 65915(p)(2).) Please 
be advised that pursuant to the recent enactment of AB 2097, the City cannot impose any minimum 
parking requirements on the Project, which is located within one-half mile of public transit. (Gov. Code 
§ 65863.2.) The Project currently proposes 76 Parking spaces within the building.  
 
As a brief introduction to our firm, Prometheus owns and/or manages over 13,000 apartment homes on 
the west coast and is the largest private owner of apartments in the Bay Area. Prometheus is a long- 
term owner and operator, having built its first project in Sunnyvale back in 1968. Two of Prometheus’ 
most recent projects are in the City of San Mateo, 303 Baldwin (the former Trags site and 1st and B). 
Prometheus Real Estate Group is a local firm with our headquarters in Downtown San Mateo. 
We appreciate your consideration of this request and look forward to working with you and the City on

Subject: 
Applicability of AB 130 CEQA Exemption to the Gateway/668 E. 3rd Ave., San 
Mateo Project 
On June 30, 2025, a new statutory CEQA exemption for multifamily housing development 
projects was enacted as part of Assembly Bill 130 (“AB 130”) and became effective immediately. 
(See Pub. Res. Code § 21080.66.) The new AB 130 statutory CEQA exemption is similar to the 
existing categorical Class 32 exemption under the CEQA Guidelines, except that AB 130: 1) 
accommodates larger residential projects; 2) reduces legal risks by limiting opportunity for third party 
challenges (no “unusual circumstances” challenges are permitted); and 3) creates a strict project 
approval timeline starting with application completeness. 
This memorandum reviews the application materials for the Gateway Project (“Project”) 
proposed at 668 E. 3rd Ave., San Mateo, California (“Property”) to determine the applicability of the 
new AB 130 CEQA exemption to the Project. Additionally, this memorandum briefly outlines how 
the streamlined approval timeline will impact the Project. We note that unlike the Class 32 
Exemption, an analysis of potential impacts related to traffic, noise, air quality, and water quality will 
not be required to support the exemption. Instead, the project site must meet all of the SB 35 siting 
criteria (see below). Therefore, qualifying housing development projects should be processed much 
more quickly since technical studies should not be required, with the possible exception of a desktop 
biological resources survey.  
 As we explain below, the Project qualifies for the AB 130 CEQA exemption. We recommend 
that this memorandum be shared with the City of San Mateo (“City”) before the Project application is 
deemed complete (or Prometheus notifies the City that it qualifies for AB 130) so that the City will 
be in a position to timely initiate the mandatory tribal consultation process, discussed in Section II 
below.

I. 
NEW CEQA EXEMPTION ELIGIBILITY REQUIREMENTS 
To qualify for the AB 130 CEQA exemption, the project must satisfy specific site and project 
requirements. Unlike other housing streamlining laws enacted in recent years, AB 130 does not 
contain any affordability requirements, and labor requirements are limited to only a narrow class of 
projects, none of which fit the description for the Project. As described below, the Project fits each of 
the AB 130 qualifying criteria. 
a. Housing project. The project must be a housing development project, which is 
defined to include: (1) projects consisting of residential uses only; (2) mixed-use 
projects where at least two-thirds of the new or converted square footage is designated 
for residential use; (3) mixed-use projects with greater than 500 units where at least 
half of the new or converted square footage is designated for residential use and other 
specific requirements are met; (4) transitional housing or supportive housing; and (5) 
farmworker housing. (Gov. Code §§ 65589.5(h)(2), 65905.5(b); Pub. Res. Code 
§ 21080.66(a).)  
The Project meets this requirement because, as described in the Project application, it 
will be developed with 100% residential uses. 
b. Acreage. The project site must be 20 acres or less, except Builder’s Remedy project 
sites must be 5 acres or less. (Pub. Res. Code § 21080.66(a)(1).) 
The Project meets this requirement because it is not a Builder’s Remedy project and 
the Property is 0.64 acres. 
c. Urban area. The project site must be within the boundaries of an incorporated 
municipality or in an urban area, as defined by the U.S. Census Bureau. (Pub. Res. 
Code § 21080.66(a)(2).) 
The Project meets this requirement because it is within the City of San Mateo, an 
incorporated municipality. 
d. Infill location. The project site must be an urban infill site, meaning that: (i) the site 
was previously developed with an urban use; (ii) at least 75% of the perimeter of the 
site adjoins parcels that are developed with urban uses; (iii) at least 75% of the area 
within a one-quarter mile radius of the site is developed with urban uses; or (iv) for 
sites with four sides, at least three sides are developed with urban uses and at least

--- page 163 ---
To: Prometheus Real Estate Group 
From: David H. Blackwell 
Date:  October 9, 2025 
Page 3 
 
 
4912-3999-1130.5/  
372819-00029/10-9-25/dhb/dhb 
 
 
two-thirds of the perimeter of the site adjoins parcels that are developed with urban 
uses. (Pub. Res. Code § 21080.66(a)(3).) 
The Project meets this requirement because the Property is currently developed with a 
retail center, which qualifies as an “urban use.” The Property also qualifies under the 
other definitions of urban infill site because it is surrounded on at least 75% of the 
perimeter, or three of four sides, by urban uses. 
e. Environmental siting criteria. The project must meet environmental siting criteria 
set forth in SB 35/423. To qualify, a site must not be located in any of the following: 
1) certain areas of the coastal zone; 2) prime farmland, farmland of statewide 
importance, or land designated for agricultural protection or preservation; 3) wetlands; 
4) a very high fire hazard severity zone (unless certain mitigation measures adopted); 
5) a hazardous waste site; 6) a delineated earthquake fault zone; 7) a 100-year flood 
hazard area or regulatory floodway; 8) lands identified for conservation or under a 
conservation easement; or 9) habitat for protected species. (Pub. Res. Code 
§ 21080.66(a)(6); Gov. Code § 65913.4(a)(6).) 
The Project meets this requirement because the Property does not fall within any of 
the prohibited categories. Specifically: 
i. The Property is not within the coastal zone; 
ii. The Property is not on land used or designated for agriculture; 
iii. The Property is not on a wetland; 
iv. The Property is not within a very high fire hazard severity zone, per our review 
of the Office of the State Fire Marshal’s Fire Hazard Severity Zone maps; 
v. The Property is not on a hazardous waste site, per our review of the Cortese 
List of hazardous waste sites; 
vi. The Property is not within a delineated earthquake fault zone, per our review 
of the California Department of Conservation’s Earthquake Hazards Zone 
Application; 
vii. The Property is not within a 100-year flood hazard area nor a regulatory 
floodway, per our review of FEMA’s National Flood Hazard Layer Viewer;

From: David H. Blackwell

viii. The Property is not on lands identified for conservation or subject to a 
conservation easement; 
ix. The Property is not habitat for protected species. 
f. Land use regulations. The project must be consistent with the applicable general plan 
and zoning ordinance, as well as any applicable local coastal program. If the general 
plan and zoning ordinance are inconsistent, the project need only be consistent with 
one. Use of any State Density Bonus Law density bonus, incentive or concession, 
waiver, or reduced parking ratio shall not be grounds to determine the project is 
inconsistent with the zoning, general plan, or local coastal program. The housing 
development shall be deemed consistent if there is substantial evidence that would 
allow a reasonable person to conclude as such. (Pub. Res. Code § 21080.66(a)(4).) 
The Project meets this requirement because it is consistent with the land use 
designations for the Property. The Property is designated “Mixed Use Medium II” in 
the City’s 2040 General Plan and is within the Central Business Support (“CBD-S”) 
zoning district. The Mixed Use Medium II designation permits a mix of uses, including 
residential, with a maximum density range of 51 - 99 dwelling units per acre. The 
CBD-S zoning district permits residential uses subject to R3 or R4 district minimum 
development standards and CBD residential development standards. The CBD-S 
district permits a maximum of 50 dwelling units per acre. This is inconsistent with the 
minimum density of the Mixed Use Medium II general plan designation. Under AB 
130, if the general plan and zoning are inconsistent, then the project shall be deemed 
consistent with both if it is consistent with one. 
Per the Project application, the residential density will be 99 dwelling units per acre 
which is within the General Plan range for the Property. Because the Project is 
consistent with the General Plan, it is deemed consistent with the applicable zoning 
district. Further, because the Project qualifies for a density bonus, any development 
standards that would preclude development of the Project as designed, such as the R3, 
R4, or CBD residential development standards, will be waived or reduced. 
g. Minimum density. The proposed residential density must be at least 50% of the 
minimum residential density deemed appropriate to accommodate housing for the 
jurisdiction. Depending on the type of jurisdiction (nonmetropolitan, suburban, or 
metropolitan), the minimum density ranges from 5 to 15 units per acre. (Gov. Code § 
65583.2(c)(3)(B); Pub. Res. Code § 21080.66(a)(5).)

The Project meets this requirement because, with a proposed density of 99 dwelling 
units per acre, it has a greater density than the highest statutory minimum density of 
15 units per acre. 
h. Historic structures. The project does not require the demolition of a historic structure 
that was placed on a national, state, or local historic register before the date a 
preliminary application (as defined) was submitted. (Pub. Res. Code 
§ 21080.66(a)(7).) 
The Project meets this requirement because none of the existing structures to be 
demolished are on a national, state, or local historic register. 
i. Freeway proximity. For any housing within 500 feet of a freeway, the building: (i) 
must have a centralized heating, ventilation, and air-conditioning system and the 
outdoor intakes for that system cannot face the freeway; (ii) must provide air filtration 
media for outside and return air that provide a minimum efficiency reporting value of 
16, which must be replaced as specified; and (iii) must not have any balconies facing 
the freeway. (Pub. Res. Code § 21080.66(c)(2).) 
The project is not within 500 feet of a freeway.  
j. Tribal notice. The City must notify all California Native American tribes that are 
traditionally and culturally affiliated with the project site, and consult with any tribe 
that elects to be involved, as specified in the statute. Related conditions of project 
approval may be imposed. (Pub. Res. Code § 21080.66(b).) 
During preparation of the EIR for the 2040 General Plan, the City identified the 
following tribes as potentially having local knowledge: 1) Amah Mutsun Tribal Band 
of Mission San Juan Bautista; 2) Costanoan Rumsen Carmel Tribe; 3) Indian Canyon 
Mutsun Band of Costanoan; 4) Muwekma Ohlone Indian Tribe of the SF Bay Area; 5) 
The Ohlone Indian Tribe; and 6) Wuksache Indian Tribe/Eshom Valley Band. Of 
these, only the Canyon Mutsun Band of Costanoan Ohlohne People responded. 
Therefore, it is possible that this tribe will respond to a consultation request for the 
Project. 
k. Phase I environmental site assessment. A Phase I Environmental Site Assessment 
(“ESA”) must be performed for the project site, and if a recognized environmental 
condition is found, certain steps must be taken to ensure there is no threat to human 
health or safety, as specified in the statute. (Pub. Res. Code § 21080.66(c)(1).)

A Phase I ESA for the Property was prepared for Prometheus Real Estate Group on 
June 6, 2025. The report identified three Recognized Environmental Conditions 
(“RECs”): 1) the presence of fuel-related impacts in sub-surface media due to 
upgradient gasoline/service stations (one of which received regulatory closure in 
2015, the other in 2021); 2) a vapor encroachment condition from offsite sources of 
TPHg and benzene; and 3) the presence of lead in shallow soil. The Phase I did not 
identify any Controlled Recognized Environmental Conditions (“CRECs”), Historical 
Recognized Environmental Conditions (“HRECs”), Business Environmental Risks 
(“BERs”), de minimis conditions, or significant data gaps.  
Significant fuel-related impacts were not identified in shallow soil and were only 
present in soil collected 20 feet below ground surface or deeper. The Phase I also 
noted that oxygen levels in the soil have created a bioattenuation zone beneath the 
property and that vapor mitigation for the current commercial land use is not 
required. The report stated that the lead levels identified at the site were 
“commonplace” in the region, were not characterized as a California or Federal 
Hazardous Waste, and did not extent further down than five feet. 
Due to the identified RECs, Prometheus will prepare a Preliminary Endangerment 
Assessment, as defined in Health & Safety Code Section 78095, to determine if a 
hazardous substance has been released on the site and what the potential exposure is 
for future occupants. A Preliminary Endangerment Assessment is currently being 
prepared by Citadel EHS, and no concerns have been identified to date.  Regardless, 
this document will be reviewed by the San Mateo County Groundwater Protection 
Program, which will determine whether significant mitigation or ongoing 
management will be required by the County. Upon receipt of the County’s approval, 
the City may issue a certificate of occupancy.  
Note that the presence of RECs on the Property in no way affects the applicability or 
timing of the AB 130 CEQA exemption. The only result is an obligation for 
Prometheus to address the RECs prior to receipt of a certificate of occupancy. 
l. Transient lodging. For new projects “deemed complete” on or after January 1, 2025, 
no portion of the project may be designated for use as transient lodging (as defined). 
“Deemed complete” means that an SB 330 preliminary application or a complete 
application (pursuant to Gov. Code § 65943) has been submitted for the project. (Pub. 
Res. Code § 21080.66(a)(8).) 
The Project meets this requirement because none of the proposed components will be 
used for transient lodging.

m. Labor requirements. Any building over 85 feet in height (from grade) is subject to 
the SB 35 labor standards, including prevailing wage requirements, recordkeeping 
requirements, additional labor standards for developments over 50 units, and 
additional skilled and trained workforce requirements. (Pub. Res. Code 
§ 21080.66(d)(2); see Gov. Code § 65913.4(a)(8).) All construction workers employed 
in the execution of public or private housing development projects where 100% of 
units will be dedicated to lower income households shall be paid prevailing wages; 
registered apprentices may be paid the applicable apprentice prevailing rate. (Pub. 
Res. Code § 21080.66(d)(1).) 
The Project will not be required to comply with the above labor provisions because it 
will not be over 85 feet in height, nor will 100% of the units be dedicated to lower 
income households. 
II. 
NEW PROJECT APPROVAL TIMELINE 
AB 130 also amended the Permit Streamlining Act (“PSA”) to create a new approval timeline 
for agencies with approval authority over projects that qualify for the AB 130 CEQA exemption. 
(Gov. Code § 65950(a)(7).) The amended PSA states that an agency must approve or disapprove the 
project “[t]hirty days from the conclusion of [the tribal consultation process]” for projects invoking 
the new CEQA exemption. (Id.)  
Additionally, the tribal consultation process itself contains statutory approval timelines that, 
when combined with the new PSA provisions, establish a single approval timeline for an AB 130 
project starting with application completeness, or for applications already deemed complete, when 
the applicant notifies the City that the project qualifies for AB 130. Because the tribal consultation 
process can conclude in multiple ways, the exact timing cannot be determined from the outset. At a 
minimum, if no tribes elect to participate in the consultation, a project must be approved no later than 
104 days from the date of application completeness/AB 130 notification. If a tribe elects to 
participate in the consultation, a project must be approved no later than 178 days from the date of 
application completeness/AB 130 notification, but may be approved earlier.  
At this time, we understand the Project’s application is under review with the City Planning 
Department. Under AB 130, the approval timeline begins either when the application is deemed 
complete, or for projects with already completed applications, when the applicant notifies the City 
that the project qualifies for AB 130. (Gov. Code § 21080.66(b)(1)(A)(i)-(ii); § 65589.5(h)(5).) For 
the purposes of AB 130, “deemed complete” means the applicant has submitted an SB 330 
preliminary application. (Id.) Therefore, if a preliminary application was previously submitted for the 
Project, Prometheus can start the approval timeline immediately by notifying the City that the Project 
qualifies for AB 130. Note that the City only has 14 days from the date of application

--- page 168 ---
To: Prometheus Real Estate Group 
From: David H. Blackwell 
Date:  October 9, 2025 
Page 8 
 
 
4912-3999-1130.5/  
372819-00029/10-9-25/dhb/dhb 
 
 
completeness/AB 130 notification to provide formal notification to tribes. Therefore, we recommend 
informing the City as soon as possible that the Project will utilize the AB 130 CEQA exemption to 
ensure that there are no delays once the application is deemed complete or Prometheus makes an AB 
130 notification. As stated above, at least one tribe participated in the preparation of the 2024 General 
Plan, so it is possible that the Project may go through this consultation process.

RECOMMENDED MODIFICATIONS TO 
CONDITIONS OF APPROVAL
48(d) CURB AND GUTTER – The applicant shall replace to existing City standards all 
curb and gutter surrounding fronting the project site and as required for restoration 
purposes. New curb and gutter shall be constructed per current City Standard, or as 
otherwise shown on the approved plan set.

--- page 199 ---
RECOMMENDED MODIFICATIONS TO 
CONDITIONS OF APPROVAL
48(m) TRAFFIC SIGNAL INFRASTRUCTURE – The applicant shall be responsible for updating the 
traffic signal at the easterly corner of the Delaware Street & 3rd Avenue intersection to the latest 
standards and requirements. The applicant shall submit all necessary traffic signal design plans, 
including pole and conductor schedules where necessary, to the Director of Public Works or 
designee for review and approval as part of the Building Permit for the Superstructure. The plans 
shall show all traffic signal equipment upgrades for the traffic signal at the easterly corner of the 
Delaware Street & 3rd Avenue intersection to comply with latest California Manual on Uniform 
Traffic Control Devices (CA MUTCD), Caltrans, and City standards requirements.  Improvements 
shall include, but are not limited to accessible pedestrian signals (APS) and pushbuttons (PPB), 
emergency vehicle preemption signal equipment, video detection equipment, 12” LED signal 
diodes, intersection PTZ camera, signal head backplates, internally illuminated street name signs, 
traffic signal interconnect or fiber optic communications. APS upgrades shall be installed on all 
corners of the Delaware Street & 3rd Avenue intersection.

--- page 200 ---
RECOMMENDED MODIFICATIONS TO 
CONDITIONS OF APPROVAL
48(n) STREET LIGHT(S) AND INFRASTRUCTURE – The applicant shall furnish and install 
necessary infrastructure in accordance with a  the photometric analysis prepared as part 
of the approved planning application superstructure permit. The streetlight and 
electrical plans shall show all electrical conduits, pull boxes, service connections, fuse 
holders, bus fuses and all other electrical components necessary to construct the 
improvements. The plans shall be submitted as part of the Building Permit for the 
Superstructure.
If any changes to streetlight locations or quantities are proposed during the 
building permit phase, a new photometric analysis shall be prepared by the 
applicant for review and approval by the Director of Public Works or 
designee and the lighting shall be furnished and installed in accordance with 
the new photometric analysis as approved.

--- page 201 ---
STAFF RECOMMENDATION
Recommend that the City Council adopt a resolution to approve 
the Site Plan and Architectural Review (SPAR), and Site 
Development Planning Application (SDPA) for the construction of a 
new multi-family residential building with 128 units and associated 
site improvements at 668 East 3rd Avenue, and find that the 
Project is Statutorily Exempt from the California Environmental 
Quality Act (CEQA) pursuant to Assembly Bill 130, based on the 
findings for approval and subject to the conditions of approval, 
with the recommended modifications.

ARCHITECTURAL CONCEPT

--- page 211 ---
•	 7 of 13 Spanish 
Revival architectural 
elements are 
required in the ODS 
specific plans. [7.1.2, 
7.7.2]
•	 The architecture  
incorporates 8 of the 
elements into the 
design.
	
1. Multi-level roofs
	
2. Asymmetrical massing
	
3. Arches
	
4. Ornamental details
	
5. Spiral columns
	
6. Multi-pane windows
	
7. Window grilles
	
8. Elaborate chimney tops
	
9. Round or square towers
	
10. Decorative tiles
	
11. Decorative ironwork
	
12. Ornamental door/	
	
	
      window surrounds
	
13. Deep recessed openings

Re: Proposed Housing Development Project at 668 East 3rd Avenue  
 
Dear San Mateo Planning Commission, 
 
The California Housing Defense Fund (“CalHDF”) submits this letter to remind the City of its 
obligation to abide by all relevant state laws when evaluating the proposed 128-unit housing 
development project at 668 East 3rd Avenue, which includes 10 very low-income units, and 
10 moderate-income units. These laws include the Housing Accountability Act (“HAA”), the 
Density Bonus Law (“DBL”), and AB 130. 
 
The HAA provides the project legal protections. It requires approval of zoning and general 
plan compliant housing development projects unless findings can be made regarding 
specific, objective, written health and safety hazards. (Gov. Code, § 65589.5, subds. (d.), (j).) 
The HAA also bars cities from imposing conditions on the approval of such projects that 
would reduce the project’s density (id. at subd. (j)) or render the project infeasible (id. at subd. 
(d)) unless, again, such written findings are made. As a development with at least two-thirds 
of its area devoted to residential uses, the project falls within the HAA’s ambit, and it 
complies with local zoning code and the City’s general plan.  Increased density, concessions, 
and waivers that a project is entitled to under the DBL (Gov. Code, § 65915) do not render the 
project noncompliant with the zoning code or general plan, for purposes of the HAA (Gov. 
Code, § 65589.5, subd. (j)(3)).  The HAA’s protections therefore apply, and the City may not 
reject the project except based on health and safety standards, as outlined above. 
Furthermore, if the City rejects the project or impairs its feasibility, it must conduct “a 
thorough analysis of the economic, social, and environmental effects of the action.” (Id. at 
subd. (b).)  
 
 
2201 Broadway, PH1, Oakland, CA 94612 
www.calhdf.org

--- page 244 ---
CalHDF also writes to emphasize that the DBL offers the proposed development certain
protections. The City must respect these protections. In addition to granting the increase in
residential units allowed by the DBL, the City must not deny the project the proposed
concessions and waivers with respect to height, blank walls, setbacks, stepbacks, entries, and
parking. If the City wishes to deny requested waivers, Government Code section 65915,
subdivision (e)(1) requires findings that the waivers would have a specific, adverse impact
upon health or safety, and for which there is no feasible method to satisfactorily mitigate or
avoid the specific adverse impact. If the City wishes to deny requested concessions,
Government Code section 65915, subdivision (d)(1) requires findings that the concessions
would not result in identifiable and actual cost reductions, that the concessions would have
a specific, adverse impact on public health or safety, or that the concessions are contrary to
state or federal law. The City, if it makes any such findings, bears the burden of proof. (Gov.
Code, § 65915, subd. (d)(4).) Of note, the DBL specifically allows for a reduction in required
accessory parking in addition to the allowable waivers and concessions. (Id. at subd. (p).)
Additionally, the California Court of Appeal has ruled that when an applicant has requested
one or more waivers and/or concessions pursuant to the DBL, the City “may not apply any
development standard that would physically preclude construction of that project as
designed, even if the building includes ‘amenities’ beyond the bare minimum of building
components.’ (Bankers Hill 150 v. City of San Diego (2022) 74 Cal.App.5th 755, 775.)

Furthermore, the project is eligible for a statutory exemption from environmental review
pursuant to section 21080.66 of the Public Resources Code. Caselaw from the California
Court of Appeal affirms that local governments err, and may be sued, when they improperly
refuse to grant a project a CEQA exemption or streamlined CEQA review to which it is
entitled. (Hilltop Group, Inc. v. County of San Diego (2024) 99 Cal.App.Sth 890, 911.)

As you are well aware, California remains in the throes of a statewide crisis-level housing
shortage. New housing such as this is a public benefit: it will provide badly needed affordable
housing; it will increase the city’s tax base; it will bring new customers to local businesses;
and it will reduce displacement of existing residents by reducing competition for existing
housing. It will also provide important housing in the heart of Silicon Valley, a region that
has seen an explosion of employment opportunities without the needed housing growth,
resulting in crippling rent burdens and housing shortages. While no one project will solve
the statewide housing crisis, the proposed development is a step in the right direction.
CalHDF urges the City to approve it, consistent with its obligations under state law.

CalHDF is a 501(c)(3) non-profit corporation whose mission includes advocating for
increased access to housing for Californians at all income levels, including low-income
households. You may learn more about CalHDF at www.calhdf.org.

Sincerely,

2of 3

MEETING DATE:
February 10, 2026 
SUBJECT:
1650-1720 S. Amphlett Boulevard - Multi-Family Residential Development (PA-2025-029)
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution approving the Site Plan and Architectural Review (SPAR), Site Development Planning Application (SDPA), 
and Vesting Tentative Map (VTM) for the construction of 256 multi-family residential units located at 1650-1720 S. Amphlett 
Boulevard, and find that the project is exempt from the California Environmental Quality Act pursuant to Public Resource 
Code 21080.66, based on the Findings for Approval and subject to Conditions of Approval. 
BACKGROUND:
On April 22, 2025, B9 Sequoia Bayshore Owner LP (applicant) submitted a formal Planning Application to demolish an existing 
office campus and construct a new multi-family residential development (“Project”) consisting of 256 for-sale residential 
units and associated site improvements. The Project consists of 192 townhome-style condominiums and 64 single-family 
detached residences.  A total of 15 percent of the housing units are designated for Moderate-Income households (38 
affordable units).
On December 20, 2024, the applicant submitted a complete Preliminary Application under Senate Bill 330, pursuant to 
Government Code Section 65589.5, prior to submitting the formal application. This vested the development to the standards 
and fee structure in effect at the time of submittal. 
SITE DESCRIPTION:
The Project site at 1650-1720 S. Amphlett Boulevard is a 14.5-acre property, currently developed with seven three-story 
office buildings and one single-story commercial building. The site is bounded by South Amphlett Boulevard to the east, 
South Grant Street to the west, Leslie Creek to the north, and the former Marriott hotel property to the south. Surrounding 
uses include single-family residences to the north and west, Bayshore (101) freeway to the east, and commercial/office uses 
to the south. The Project would demolish all existing buildings and subdivide the existing three parcels into seven new parcels 
through a vesting tentative map.
The site has a General Plan land use designation of Mixed-Use Medium I and a zoning designation of E2-1 (Executive Office).  
It is located within the Rail Corridor Transit-Oriented Development Plan Planning Area and portions of the site are within 
one-half mile of the Hayward Park Caltrain Station. Parcels within the Rail Corridor Transit-Oriented Development Plan are 
categorized as either Transit-Oriented Development (TOD) Zone parcels or Planning Area parcels. The Project site is located 
within the Planning Area, but outside of the TOD Zone. A location map showing the Project site’s vicinity is included as 
Attachment 2.
PROJECT DESCRIPTION:
The applicant proposes to construct 64 detached, three-story single-family residences primarily located on the west side of

--- page 247 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
the site along South Grant Street, and 31 townhome buildings arranged in clusters of four to eight units across four separate 
parcels with 192 units. Two main vehicular access points are proposed along South Grant Street, with additional access 
provided along South Amphlett Boulevard to serve the townhome units. Open space amenities include landscaped paseos, 
walking paths, two dog parks located on opposite sides of the site, and a centrally located 0.4-acre park. Amenities and other 
features within the central park include a shade structure, picnic tables, and play equipment. The townhome buildings are 
oriented perpendicular to South Amphlett Boulevard, with pedestrian entrances accessed from interior paseos located 
between pairs of buildings. This configuration minimizes noise and air quality impacts from the adjacent freeway on the 
residential units.
The proposed 192 townhome units range in size from approximately 1,475 to 1,755 square feet and include two- and three-
bedroom floor plans. The proposed 64 single-family residences range from approximately 2,120 to 2,250 square feet and 
include four-bedroom floor plans. Each unit is provided with an attached two-car garage, configured in either a tandem or 
side-by-side arrangement. In addition, 55 on-site visitor parking spaces are proposed. The Project also provides a series of 
public infrastructure improvements, including a curb extension and the installation of high-visibility crosswalks at the 
intersection of South Grant Street and Betty Lane, sidewalk improvements per City’s Pedestrian Master Plan, as well as the 
restriping of South Grant Street and Amphlett Boulevard to provide on-street parking. A full set of the Project plans are 
included in Attachment 3.
APPLICABLE HOUSING LAWS: 
State Density Bonus Law 
The Project utilizes the provisions of State Density Bonus Law in accordance with Government Code Section 65915 and as 
locally adopted in SMMC Chapter 27.15 Density Bonus. To comply with Density Bonus regulations, the City must allow for 
increased residential density, reduced parking standards, and “concessions” and “waivers” from development standards for 
residential projects that provide a certain percentage of units as affordable units.
The General Plan 2040 land use designation for the site is Mixed-Use Medium I, which allows a density of 50 dwelling units 
per acre or a base density of 724 units. The applicant proposes to designate 15% of the total 256 for-sale residential units to 
the Moderate-Income category, which qualifies the Project for a 10% density bonus. Because the proposed density is 
below maximum density permitted by the General Plan, the Project is not requesting a density bonus.  
 
Concession and Waiver Requests
For this Project, State Density Bonus Law also allows the applicant to request one concession and unlimited waivers from 
development standards. Generally speaking, a concession (or incentive) is a reduction or modification of a development 
standard that results in identifiable or actual cost reductions to provide for affordable housing costs, helping to make the 
Project financially feasible. (A concession also includes a reduction in site development standards or a modification of zoning 
code requirements that exceed minimum building standards, as specified.)  A waiver is a modification of a standard that 
would otherwise physically preclude the construction of the Project at the allowed density. The Project application does not 
identify any concession requests under State Density Bonus Law. However, the Project is seeking several waivers for aspects 
of the Project that do not meet various City development standards. The applicant has also included a summary of the 
Project waivers in a density bonus request letter (Attachment 5). A complete list of the Project waivers is included in 
Attachment 1, Exhibit B.
Staff have evaluated the waivers and concluded that the waivers identified are necessary to allow construction of the 
Project at the densities permitted under the City’s General Plan and State Density Bonus Law.
Other Applicable State Laws
In addition to State Density Bonus Law, there are several other State Laws that regulate housing development projects. For 
this Project, these include, but are not necessarily limited to the following:
•
The Housing Crisis Act (Senate Bill 330)
o
Under Senate Bill 330 (SB 330), the Project vests the ordinances, policies, and standards adopted and in 
effect when a preliminary application was submitted to the City. This Project submitted a Preliminary 
Application under SB 330 on December 20, 2024, and is therefore vested to the ordinances, policies, and

--- page 248 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
standards in place as of this date. 
•
The Housing Accountability Act (HAA) 
o
The HAA limits a local agency’s ability to deny, reduce the density of, or render housing development 
projects infeasible if objective standards are met. As proposed, this Project meets all applicable objective 
standards in the General Plan, Zoning Code, and other local policy documents that were in effect at the time 
the preliminary application was submitted under SB330.
•
Assembly Bill 130
o
Assembly Bill 130 (AB 130) was signed into law and became effective immediately on June 20, 2025. AB130 
included numerous changes related to housing laws, including the addition of a new statutory exemption 
from the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) for housing development projects on sites under 20 
acres that meet specific qualifying criteria. In addition to the CEQA exemption, AB130 requires the Project 
to be processed on an expedited timeline.  
City Plans, Policies and Standards
General Plan and Zoning Code
The General Plan 2040 land use designation for the site is Mixed-Use Medium I, which allows a density of 50 dwelling units 
per acre for residential development. The Project proposes 17.6 units per acre, which is within the allowable density for 
Mixed-Use Medium I. A list of applicable General Plan policies and a discussion of the Project’s conformance to them are 
included in the Resolution in Attachment 1.
The Project site is zoned E2-1 (Executive Office), which establishes development standards for floor area ratio (FAR), 
setbacks, and open space. The Project conforms to various development standards, including maximum density, setbacks, 
number of stories, parking, and loading requirements. The land use designation allows up to five stories on the site, while 
the Project proposes three-story buildings. The Project site is also located within 0.5-mile of Hayward Park Caltrain station, 
a major transit stop. Therefore, pursuant to Government Code Section 65863.2 (AB 2097), this Project is not subject to any 
minimum parking requirements. Nevertheless, the applicant is proposing to voluntarily provide a two-car garage for each 
unit as well as 55 on-site visitors parking. With approval of the requested waivers, the Project will conform to all applicable 
development standards. A Factual Data Sheet listing the applicable zoning standards and the Project’s conformance to them 
is included as Attachment 4.
Transportation Impact Analysis 
The Project is screened out of a Vehicle Miles Traveled (VMT) analysis required by the California Environmental Quality Act 
(CEQA), because the Projects located within one-half mile of a major transit stop are presumed to result in less-than-
significant transportation impacts pursuant to CEQA Guidelines Section 15064.3. 
General Plan 2040 Circulation Element Policy C 6.3 requires a site-specific transportation impact analysis prepared in 
accordance with the City’s adopted Transportation Impact Analysis (TIA) Policy for development projects that may result in 
an adverse condition or effect on the roadway system. This is a local policy requirement and is independent of CEQA VMT 
analysis. A transportation memo was prepared by the applicant’s consultant, Fehr & Peers, to demonstrate compliance with 
this General Plan Policy and the City’s Local Transportation Analysis Guidelines. The trip generation analysis indicates that 
the Project would result in a net reduction of approximately 1,700 daily vehicle trips, including a reduction of 380 trips during 
the AM peak hour (415 inbound and 35 outbound) and a reduction of 320 trips during the PM peak hour (17 inbound and 
338 outbound).
Fehr & Peers prepared a qualitative assessment of traffic conditions at three intersections based on existing travel patterns. 
Level of service (LOS) analysis was not conducted, as the proposed Project would result in a substantial decrease in vehicle 
trips. While the analysis identifies directional shifts in traffic associated with the change in land use from office to residential, 
it concludes that the Project would not result in impacts to the roadway system. The Fehr & Peers Transportation Impact 
Analysis (TIA) is included as Attachment 6.
Rail Corridor Transit-Oriented Development Plan
The Rail Corridor Plan establishes goals and policies to promote transit-oriented development within a half-mile radius of

--- page 249 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
the Hillsdale and Hayward Park Caltrain station areas. The Project site is located within one-half mile of the Hayward Park 
Caltrain Station and within the Rail Corridor Transit-Oriented Development Plan planning area. By providing consistent 
height and density, human-scale block sizes, and creating a unique and distinctive neighborhood within the plan area, the 
Project supports the Plan’s goals and policies. In addition, the Project includes significant site and streetscape improvements 
as mentioned in the project description. A full list of applicable Rail Corridor Transit-Oriented Development Plan policies and 
an analysis of the Project’s consistency are included in Attachment 1.
City’s Below Market Rate (Inclusionary) Program 
The City’s Below Market Rate (BMR) Program requires ownership projects of 11 or more units to dedicate a minimum of 15 
percent of the proposed units to the Moderate-Income category. The applicant proposes to designate 38 units (15 percent 
of the total 256 units) as Moderate-Income BMR units, including nine single-family residences and 29 townhomes. These 
affordable units are required to have access to all on-site amenities, be generally comparable in size to similar market-rate 
units, and feature exterior designs and appearances compatible with market-rate units. The Project includes a 0.4 fractional 
unit to achieve the full 15 percent requirement and is allowed to utilize the Fractional Unit Fee, as the BMR unit calculation 
results in a fractional unit of less than 0.5. The Fractional Unit Fee for the 0.4 unit will be collected and deposited into the 
City’s Affordable Housing Fund in-lieu of providing an additional affordable unit.
Multi-Family and Residential Mixed-Use Objective Design Standards
The Project is subject to the City’s Multi-Family and Residential Mixed-Use Objective Design Standards (ODS). The proposed 
architectural style is best characterized as contemporary, expressed through a combination of stucco, lap siding, and other 
materials that articulate building volumes and emphasize projections and step-backs. Traditional design elements are also 
incorporated through material selections such as asphalt shingle roofing and brick or stone veneer accents. Two color 
schemes are provided for each building type, incorporating neutral tones such as gray stucco and white siding, along with 
accent colors including green sliding panels. Overall, the buildings maintain a consistent height, unit width, and massing 
throughout the development.
The proposed buildings are three stories in height and are classified as mid-rise structures pursuant to the City’s ODS, with 
roof peaks reaching approximately 41 feet. Each unit includes a two-car garage oriented toward internal circulation streets, 
with pedestrian access provided along the rear façades via shared paseos. The units feature front porches and second-story 
balconies or sunrooms, enhancing the residential character and providing private outdoor space. Architectural articulation 
is emphasized along the side and rear façades through step-backs, projections, and façade modulation at intervals of 
approximately ten to fifteen feet. Roofline variation is similarly incorporated on these façades, adding visual interest along 
the pedestrian-oriented paseos. The Project requests several waivers from the ODS, specifically related to massing breaks, 
wall articulation, and roofline variation along the front façades facing internal streets. While the ODS requires wall 
articulation through projecting and recessed rooms and architectural projections, the buildings fronting the internal 
roadways lack sufficient wall articulation and roofline variation. Therefore, waivers from these standards are requested 
pursuant to the State Density Bonus Law. A complete list of the requested ODS waivers is provided in Attachment 1, Exhibit 
B.
Planning Applications
Site Plan and Architectural Review (SPAR)
The Project requires Site Plan and Architectural Review (SPAR) approval for the construction of a new multi-family residential 
development pursuant to San Mateo Municipal Code (“SMMC”) Section 27.08.030. The Project proposes a multi-family 
development that complements the existing architectural character of the surrounding neighborhood through the use of 
high-quality materials and extensive landscaping, which enhances the overall visual character of the site and adjacent area. 
The development will not be detrimental to the harmonious and orderly growth of the City, nor impair the desirability of 
investment or occupation in the vicinity, and otherwise is in the best interests of the public health, safety, or welfare. Overall, 
the Project design supports orderly and harmonious development of the site, complies with applicable development 
standards and General Plan policies, and would not result in adverse impacts. Details on the SPAR findings for approval are 
included in the Resolution (Attachment 1).
Site Development Planning Application (SDPA)

--- page 250 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
SMMC Section 23.40 requires a Site Development Planning Application (SDPA) approval for removal of major vegetation and 
grading of the site.  The SMMC defines “major vegetation,” as live vegetation consisting of tree growth with a trunk diameter 
of six inches or greater measured at 54 inches above natural grade. The SMMC also defines a Protected Tree as any heritage 
tree or street tree. Heritage trees include any oak tree with a minimum diameter of 10 inches measured at 54 inches above 
natural grade as well as any other species with a diameter of 15 inches measured at 54 inches above natural grade.
The Project proposes the removal of a total of 169 trees, 49 of which qualify as protected trees. All trees proposed for 
removal are located within the proposed building footprint or other site improvement areas. The equivalent landscape unit 
(LU) value of the removed trees will be replaced, as conditioned, through the planting of new trees, payment of an in-lieu 
fee, or a combination of both, in accordance with Municipal Code Section 27.71. While the Project proposes the removal of 
169 trees, the applicant also proposes approximately 620 new trees. The Project will pay an in-lieu fee to the City’s Tree 
Planting Fund to account for the remaining LU value loss, as required by code. Details regarding the SDPA findings for 
approval are provided in the Resolution (Attachment 1).
Vesting Tentative Map
The Project requires approval of a Vesting Tentative Map (VTM), pursuant to San Mateo Municipal Code Section 26.48, to 
consolidate three parcels and create seven new parcels. In addition, the Project proposes to establish individual lots for the 
single-family residences and to create condominium units for the townhomes. The final map for the proposed subdivision 
shall be obtained prior to issuance of building permits. Additional details regarding the VTM findings for approval are 
included in the Resolution. (Attachment 1).
NOTICE PROVIDED:
In accordance with Government Code Section 65090, notice of this public hearing was published in the San Mateo Daily 
Journal newspaper ten days in advance of this Planning Commission meeting. In accordance with Government Code Section 
65091 and the City’s Municipal Code noticing requirements, this public hearing was noticed to the following parties more 
than ten days in advance of this Planning Commission meeting:

•
The City’s Planning “Notify Me” email list; and, 
•
The interested parties email list, which includes interested individuals who contacted the City and requested to be 
added to the Project notification list. 
  
PUBLIC COMMENTS:
The applicant held a formal Neighborhood Informational Meeting on March 26, 2025, which was attended by approximately 
25 participants. During the formal application review, one public comment was submitted to staff, which is included as 
Attachment 8. The comment expressed concern regarding vehicles from the proposed development traveling through the 
Sunnybrae and Central neighborhoods located west of the Project site, as well as potential parking impacts on South Grant 
Street. Any public comments received after publication of this report will be forwarded to the Planning Commission for 
review and consideration at the public hearing and posted to this item on the City’s Agendas & Minutes Public Meeting 
Portal as “Post Packet Public Comments.”
FISCAL IMPACT:
As a new housing project filed under SB 330, the Project would be subject to several impact and in-lieu fees in effect at the 
time of the application filing date, including the ones listed below, which are assessed and collected prior to the issuance of 
building permits or occupancy. These estimates are exclusive of any credits that the Project may receive due to the existing 
buildings on site:
•
Child Care Development Fee of approximately $947,050 to offset the impact on the need for future childcare space 
needs by new development.
•
Park Impact Fee to offset the increased demands on park and recreation facilities serving new developments.
•
Wastewater Capacity Charge of approximately $2,650,160 to recover a proportionate share of costs for existing and 
future wastewater system facilities and assets from new or expanded connections to City wastewater systems.

--- page 251 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
•
School Impact Fees in the amount of $4.94 per sq. ft. of residential area to offset the increased demands on school 
facilities caused by new development. This is collected by the San Mateo Union High School District for all schools 
in San Mateo.
•
Landscape Unit In-Lieu Fee of approximately $1,723,2901, assessed for each Landscape Unit value not physically 
planted on-site or along street frontages.
•
Below Market Rate Fractional Unit Fee of approximately $122,800 in lieu of providing an additional affordable unit.
•
Public Art Fee in the amount of 1.19% of the total building valuation (excluding land acquisition and off-site 
improvement cost) in lieu of providing on-site public art.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
The proposed Project is exempt pursuant to Public Resource Code Section 21080.66 (AB 130) of the California Environmental 
Quality Act (CEQA) Guidelines. The Project meets the criteria for this exemption as it:
•
The site is no larger than 20 acres. 
•
The site is located within an urban area. 
•
The site has been previously developed with an urban use. 
•
The Project is consistent with the General Plan and applicable zoning regulations. 
•
The Project provides at least one-half of the density of the Housing Element’s default affordable housing zoning 
thresholds. 
•
The Project is not located within a costal zone, prime farmland or farmland of statewide importance, wetland, a very 
high fire hazard severity zone, A hazardous waste site, a delineated earthquake fault zone, a special flood hazard 
area, a regulatory floodway, Lands identified for conservation in an adopted natural community conservation plan, 
or Habitat for protected species 
•
The Project does not involve the demolition of a historic structure listed on a national, state, or local register prior 
to the application submittal. 
•
No portion of the Project is designated for use as a hotel, motel, bed and breakfast inn, or other transient lodging 
The proposed Project meets all applicable criteria and therefore qualifies for this statutory exemption. In accordance with 
Public Resources Code Section 21080.66(b)(1)(A), the City formally notified Native American tribes and invited consultation 
regarding the Project and its potential impacts on tribal cultural resources; one tribe participated in the process. On 
November 3, 2025, staff met with the Muwekma Ohlone Tribe that participated in the consultation.  In coordination with 
the tribe, Conditions of Approval have been incorporated to avoid impacts to cultural resources. Furthermore, consistent 
with Public Resources Code Section 21080.66(c), the Project is conditioned to provide a Phase I Environmental Site 
Assessment, to exclude balconies facing the freeway within 500 feet, and to implement a centralized heating and air 
conditioning system with air filtration media.

RESOLUTION NO.
